<h2>All Reviews</h2>

<ol>
    <li> I had been shaving with Norelco rotary razors for the past 10+ years and always bought the latest \\&quot;top of line\\&quot; model. I had been enticed by the amazing reviews for this Braun for the past 6 months and finally pulled the trigger to order it.    Been using it now for the past 3 weeks and must say I regret waiting so long....even with the steep price tag! Where this razor really shines is the absolute lack of skin irritation. I have sensitive skin and with the Norelco&#x27;s I would only shave mon-fri mornings before work. Never shaved on weekends or touched the 5 o&#x27;clock shadow for fear of redness and pain. However with the Braun I can now shave in morning, night, and weekends without a problem! Like others have said it can also easily handle 4-5 days growth without a problem (and I have think dark hair).    In terms of shaving closeness, the Bruan provides a closer shave on the face without question. On my neck, I would rate it about the same closeness as the Norelco (but no pulling or redness!)  I don&#x27;t find this razor louder then the Norelco models as others have mentioned. It does have to be cleaned more frequently, but this is an acceptable compromise for the results.    If you have sensitive skin, or are up in the air about this product, just buy it! You will not be sorry.</li>
    <li> Excellent shaver. My last shaver was a triple-head, that shaved it&#x27;s last shave. I was just looking for the best shaving, most reliable, durable shaver.    This one shaves very close, but still requires multiple passes and more multiple passes to get all the whiskers. The cleaning container is larger than I would have liked: It requires space on a counter near an outlet. At least one of the modes is has a rather loud re-occurring noise in the cleaning process, but it negates the need for manual cleaning. I&#x27;m very happy so far.</li>
    <li> It is an excellent shaver and good value for its price. I was using Panasonic 8047 before this but this a class above. Only problem is its refill cartridge which can&#x27;t be shipped by air being \\&quot;inflammable\\&quot;.</li>
    <li> I upgraded from a 9000 series and was blown away by how smooth it feels when shaving. My previous one felt pretty rough. I don&#x27;t notice that it shaves any closer really, but it just feels nicer when I shave and that&#x27;s good enough for me.    My one gripe with it is that the flip out cutter is smaller and not as good as the 9000 series shaver. I use it a lot when I just want to trim my facial hair rather than shave it all off.</li>
    <li> I like the way this razor works on most of my face.  It is also a comfortable shave.  My problem is that I have a very hard time getting all the hairs on my face and especially on my neck.  I actually use the Series 7 first then quickly go over my face and neck one more time with my rotary razor so I can get all the hairs I missed with the Series 7.      The cleaning / charging function of the razor is great.  It is loud but I start the cleaning on my way out the door so it doesn&#x27;t bother me.</li>
    <li> Perfect in every way!  I cannot say anything bad about this shaver!  Simply perfect.</li>
    <li> I have been using Braun shavers for the past 10 years, and every time they come up with a new series, I am usually skeptical on how much improvement one would get in shaving performance for shelling out money for a new shaver. This time, however, I was pleasantly surprised. This shaver is definitely a notch above my previous 8995 version. They have re-designed the shaver head, which gives a closer shave, and the battery lasts longer as well. The only downside to Braun shavers is that they sell their proprietary cleaning solution at ridiculous margins(much like how the printer manufacturers sell you their proprietary Ink cartridges).</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using electric shavers for nearly 20 years, and this is the best one I&#x27;ve ever purchased. It is very comfortable, both during and after shaving. It shaves quickly and closely without any mess. I like everything about this product so far, and would recommend it to anyone who&#x27;s looking for a great electric shaver. It is pricey, but this is an example of getting what you pay for.</li>
    <li> I have the 9595 Pulsonic model for more than a year.  I may have rushed too early to buy it, and the design flaws I see may have been fixed by now...    I have been using Braun shavers for over 30 years, so my experience with this one is terribly disappointing. Here are the design flaws I see:  * The contacts at the back do not make good contact with the charging/cleaning base. When the shaver starts the cleaning cycle, quite often the contacts separate, and both cleaning and charging stop in the middle, leaving the shaver soaked in the cleaning fluid.  * The beard trimmer simply fell off after about 5 months.  * There is a bad contact inside the shaver that randomly stops it in mid shave. This never manifests itself when I take it to the lab (of course...)  I think that the engine is simply too powerful for the rest of the shaver and base.    The shaver shaves well, but is hard to clean without the base, and the base is just plain bad design.  I&#x27;m really at a loss what shaver to get now. Is this model indicative of the quality level of Braun shavers these days?</li>
    <li> I have had the old Braun Flex shaver for years and wanted to update. On a recent trip to Germany, I thought I&#x27;d get one there.  NOT !  The Euro stopped that very quickly. At approx. $1.50 per Euro, and the price there being E 300 (that&#x27;s about $450), I passed on that option immediately.  Bought it on Amazon for $220.    The only thing more satisfying than getting my Braun Pulsonic at half the price....is that it is everthing I expected and more. A smooth, close shave and a cleaning system which leaves me \\&quot;ready to go\\&quot; anytime I need to shave. Execellent.....</li>
    <li> This is without question the best shaver providing the best shave I have experienced.  I had a top of the line Braun shaver for 10 years which just stopped working.  I was somewhat skeptical of the reviews for this shaver but it has performed as the best reviews have suggested.  You won&#x27;t be dissappointed.  Amazon was the best price found for this product...I saved over $50 off compared with our local WalMarts store.</li>
    <li> Been a electric razor user for 12 years.. I typically change shaver once in 4 years. My first one was a braun foil. Liked it. My next one was a Norelco rotary top end model..Liked it and swore would never go to foil again.. But as I was looking at upgrading to norelco aztec, i saw these piled up positive reviews on amazon for this foil razor.. Then I did my research and said i would give it a try.     I must say this pulsonic shaver got converted me to foil once again.. awesome performance.. Far exceeded my expectations..  I thought that auto-cleaning stuff was unnecessary as i was used to tap cleaing. But now i am addicted to it..If i want to nitpick on one, that would be the travel case.. looks cheap. But that is not the important point here. Hey, I wanted a good shaver for the price - Braun delivered it, making my daily shaving chore a pleasure..thanks..</li>
    <li> I have had the Braun 790 for about a month now and I am extremely happy with my daily shave. No, I don&#x27;t work for the company just a happy user. I have been using an electric razor for about 15 years. Norelco has been my brand of choice and have had ok results but needed to skip every couple of days or my face would be sore. So decided I would try another brand this time. Based on the reviews selected the Braun. Can&#x27;t speak about the newer Norelcos they may give just as good a shave but Consumer Reports magazine and the various comments rated this one highly.    What do I like?  -the closest shave I have ever gotten from an electric razor  -close shave every time whether I wash my face first or use the razor first as the company suggest  -no sore neck or face using it daily  -nice cleaning stand that does a fine job  -used on a trip and running hot water on the head seemed to do fine as well  -low energy use when cleaning when I checked it with my watt killer meter    Any concern?  -so far none to speak of  -I am still working on getting the shave on my upper lip as close as I would like. But I am figuring it out  -some mentioned the case not as handy as just a cap over the cutting blade for travel but I have found the case is just fine. same size as razor so no space difference    I am a happy camper so if it changes I will be back  with another post.    This razor is well worth the price.</li>
    <li> Over the years I have used both blades and other makes of electric shavers.  However, after doing my homework in researching a quality product.  I found it with the Braun Series 7 - 790cc Pulsonic Shaver.  It is a major improvement over what I have used in the past giving me a good clean shave.  I highly recommend the product.  However, keep in mind its a little pricey but worth the extra money.    Emanuel Stein</li>
    <li> I have been using a Norelco electric for the last 20+ years but have always had occasional problems with ingrown hairs which have gotten worse recently.  So I decided to try out a Braun to see if it would do better.  At first I was having HORRIBLE problems with ingrown hairs on the Braun, I was getting a couple nasty ones every week, real nasty ones.  My neck looked like a minefield.  Just when I was about to give up I decided to try a different shaving technique.  With my old Norelco I had to make many quick passes to get all the hairs cut so that was the way I was doing it with this one.  I decided to try slowing down, and found that the vibrating head in fact made it possible to shave that way and get just as quick a shave in the end because only a couple passes were needed.  To get an idea of the speed, I now take about three seconds to run up a side cheek on my face.  Now as you have probably guessed already, that has completely solved my ingrown hair problem and I am now doing much better than I did with my old Norelco.    I have found the self-cleaning aspect handy.  I was initially concerned that I would be spending far too much money on the replacement liquid things that go in the base, but after four months of use I am still on the same one so it looks like 2-3 per year which isn&#x27;t all that horrible.    Scott</li>
    <li> Alrighty then. I&#x27;ve had Braun razors ever since I was over playing Army in Germany in the mid- 80&#x27;s. At that time I bought a battery powered Braun for the field. It worked well then, and worked fine until I moved about three years ago and misplaced it. It&#x27;s around here somewhere, and I&#x27;ve no doubt that it&#x27;ll still work fine when I finally stumble across it someday.      Anyway, the razor that this new 790cc replaces is the 8985 360 degree complete, which still works fine, but with which I&#x27;ve grown bored. I&#x27;m sending it to my little brother (he still gets my hand-me-downs, but never complains!) where it will no doubt continue to perform well.     How does the 790 perform? In a word: peerlessly.  It powers through my not insubstantial beard with no audible slowing (generations prior to the 8985 would bog down if I tried to shave too quickly) and without having to go over the same spot several times.  It even cleans up the throat and neck area quickly and comfortably.  And... I shave my head with it and it works very, very well for that too!        I tried the 500 series Braun: not bad, but not as good as my three year old 8985.  It went back.  I tried the top-of-the-line Norelco triple head razor. Lift and cut shaving? What a crock! I&#x27;d finish with the the Norelco and go over the same area with the 8985. Smoother. The Norelco went back. So, enough screwing around!  What&#x27;s the top Braun? 790cc. I bought it and am very happy.     Notable features and differences from previous generation Braun razors:    This one can be rinsed in warm water to clean it if you don&#x27;t want to use the clean and renew station. Nice, but make sure you pop off the screen /  cutter block to dry, off of the razor. If you put it in the cleaning station to dry, it won&#x27;t, and you&#x27;ll get a cold wet razor the next time you fire it up. Yuck.     The trimmer is a new design from previous razors, and I actually prefer the old style.  This one works, but it&#x27;s weaker than previously (it will bog if you tryto go too quickly) and is harder to be precise with. I have a long sweeping mustache and if I have to mess with it, I&#x27;ll typically reach for my dedicated trimmer.      The cutter block and screen have been combined into one unit. I like it actually, as it seems to better contain the shaved material. (Remember that I shave my head, too?).  I read a review (complaint?) on here that it was more expensive to replace than before, but no, a little e-shopping and you&#x27;ll find that it&#x27;s the same as replacing the screen and cutter block. They work together, get dull together, and should  be replaced at the same time. If your scissor gets dull, you don&#x27;t sharpen one blade, right? Same principle.      This razor is powered by a lithium polymer battery, where prevoiusly they were powered with nickel metal hydride batts.  I wish they&#x27;d have stayed with the nimh, as I believe that they have a much longer lifespan. I actually think that the battery will be the longevity limiting factor with this razor.  Will I grow bored with this razor and be looking for the next generation, better Braun before the battery croaks? I&#x27;m not so sure.  Maybe they can re-power it a service center.    The razor has an LCD display on the bottom that shows remaining battery power, and the cleanliness of the razor. Pretty nifty. Each scale (six segments in a little curved line) gets reset when the Clean and Renew station is used to clean/lubricate and charge the razor (Like having a brand new razor each time!), but not when it&#x27;s rinsed in warm water.  That&#x27;s another complaint that people make: you have to pay for the cartridges to refill the cleaning station.  Whoopie doo. They last about two months each, and they cost about ten bucks for two.  A little over two bucks a month to keep it in tip top shape. Again, whoopie doo. You don&#x27;t have to use the station, but why buy this razor at all if you don&#x27;t plan on using the cleaning function?    To finish, I would whole-heartedly recommend this razor to anyonewho wants a smooth, non irritating shave. Is it as close as a good blade? Nope. It can&#x27;t be. As thin as they make the screen, it&#x27;s still there, and it&#x27;s between the cutter and your skin. But it&#x27;s darned close, and I don&#x27;t believe there&#x27;s a better electric out there anywhere!</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve owned two electrics razors, both Norelco&#x27;s.     <li> This review is for the Braun 7-790cc electric shaver.  Highly recommended.  Worth every penny.    The last foil shaver I tried was a really old model which my grandfather left to me, about 10 years ago.  I tried it once and brutally cut up my face. I ended up having to finish up some parts of my face with a razor.  Also, the tradeoff for setting the shaver for a reasonably close shave was that my skin would often get irritated, especially since I would have to do multiple passes to try to do a somewhat reasonable job.  It was time to purchase a new shaver, and I considered purchasing this model, but I was nervous, because of the expense, and because it would be my first foil shaver.    I read the reviews of the Braun and decided to give it a try.    I have been satisfied with the closeness of the Braun shave, and extremely satisfied with the comfortable shave and the ease of cleaning.  I started off the first few weeks being very gentle and careful with the shaver, not pressing too hard.  It is recommended that you stretch the skin and hold the shaver perpendicular to your face.  After a few weeks, I became more comfortable with the shaver and started to press harder.  I recently got my very first nick with the shaver.  I had stretched the skin, but apparently pressed a little too hard, and I felt it nick me right on the end of my chin.  It was just a very small nick with a little bead of blood.  Not bad at all, and I&#x27;m pretty sure I can avoid it in the future just by not pressing as hard around the bony contours of my jaw.    This shaver does not shave as close as a blade, but it does a fairly good job, and I believe it does the best job possible for an electric shaver.    The cleaning cartridges make me a little uncomfortable, because I don&#x27;t know exactly what they contain.  I believe it is alcohol plus some lubricants.  I&#x27;m not sure whether it qualifies as hazardous waste.  Each cartridge costs about $6 and lasts about a month (of daily cleanings).  You can subscribe via Amazon.com, so that you will receive a package of 2 new cartridges every 2 months, and you will get free shipping and a 15% discount by doing so.  The cleaning system activates the shaver and draws the cleaning solution from the cartridge into the shaver, in order to flush it out.  The noise of the cleaning system is a little bit annoying, due to a high-pitched whine, but I am fairly sensitive to those sorts of noises.  It&#x27;s acceptable to me (and my cat), so I don&#x27;t think this would be a deal-breaker for the great majority of people.  You would not want to start the cleaning cycle while your partner is trying to sleep in the next room.  After cleaning, the next day there sometimes seems to be a very small amount of alcohol/lubricant residue on the shaver itself, and a little bit of odor from the cleaning system, but it&#x27;s not bothersome.  It is quite a luxury not to have to clean the shaver manually (although it is possible to do so while traveling and away from the cleaning center).    Here are the cleaning cartridges, which are available from Amazon.com (free shipping via Amazon Prime or by subscribing to the product):    [[ASIN:B000050FDY Braun Clean &amp; Renew Refills (2 Pack)]]    My particular model (7-790cc) has a fast cleaning cycle, which I doubt I will ever use.  The reason is that I don&#x27;t want to use the shaver immediately after it has been cleaned, because I&#x27;m concerned that the used cleaning solution may not have completely drained or evaporated from the shaver.    I am hoping that by cleaning the shaver regularly and replacing the foil and cutters every 18 months, it will keep shaving this well for years to come.  I&#x27;m very happy I tried out this foil shaver.  I shave every day, which makes my partner happy.  I look better.  My face doesn&#x27;t get all red and irritated.  I don&#x27;t have to finish up with a razor.  I do have to do multiple passes on my neck, and particularly on my sideburns for some reason, in order to find the best angle to approach the hair, but this doesn&#x27;t bother me, because my face doesn&#x27;t get irritated.  I think it takes me about 5 minutes to shave, and it&#x27;s a very comfortable experience without any fear of nicks, cuts, or irritation.    The shaver itself also looks very impressive.</li>

    <li> First, I should point out that I&#x27;m not an electric shaver type of guy.  Every time I bought one (typically the cheap $50 kind in a Target store), it irritated my skin and didn&#x27;t get a close shave, and so I would return it.  I love manual razors, I can get every whisker, and I generally can do it without cuts.  The problem is that it does hurt, if minimally, and I thought why not give electrics one more try.    Second, I have thick facial hair.  I don&#x27;t let it grow more than 5 days because by then the stubble gets unbearably itchy and I don&#x27;t like how I look with a beard or mustache.  This may be true of most faces (what do I know), but my facial hair also grows in different directions.  For instance, hair on my face is pretty simple (grows down) but hair on my neck generally grows diagonally down away from the chin (with some fun exceptions that take a few rubs of the fingertips to figure out the best angle to shave at those trouble spots).  I also lift my chin to get my neck skin taught to shave, and around the jawline I sometimes like to tilt my head up or down to move my jawbone a few inches underneath my skin so I have a hard surface to shave my jawline against (makes it easier to use less pressure and thus not cut myself).  Again, manual razors do the trick relatively easily (now that I know which direction to shave on different parts of my face) although I&#x27;d prefer to avoid the minimal discomfort that comes with a manual.  WHICH IS TO SAY, i have no doubt that your experience with this razor may be much more positive if your don&#x27;t get much facial hair.    Enter the Braun Series 7 - 790cc.  I decided, hey, if I&#x27;m going to really give this a shot, I should get the best, and, let&#x27;s face it, everyone on the internet seems to be falling over themselves to point out how perfect this shaver is compared to its competition (generally people seem to agree that foil shavers are superior to rotary, particularly for more coarse hair, and that dry shavers are better than one&#x27;s for the shower -- and this has been claimed by many to be the best dry foil shaver on the market by far).  I also read up on the art of electric shaving, including the importance of a dry face (yes, I tried Lectric Shave liquid a few times, as some recommend to dry the face), the possible value of showering first and then drying your face before shaving, using the shaver well over a month to allow your face to adjust to it, doing the trouble spots first (in my case below my jawline) before the shaver head gets warm and thus more irritating to the skin, and pulling skin taught where necessary during shaving.    THE GENERAL PROBLEM WITH THIS SHAVER -- for me at least, given my facial hair type -- is that it shaves my face perfectly but, starting just above the jaw line, it misses a large number of long hairs.  Imagine, if you will, a nearly perfect shave (my god it does my cheeks and mustache like it got waxed or something, that was kind of awesome) on my whole face, except there are 50 or so longish hairs in random spots starting just above my jaw line and continuing down my neck.  It looks absolutely ridiculous!  Believe me, I ran the shaver over those bad boys in every way I could think, every angle, every pressure, multiple times.  I even took a tweezer to try to pull those hairs away from my skin to see if the shaver would then have an easier time catching them, all to no avail.    So ultimately every time I used that shaver I&#x27;d have to do a follow-up shave with a manual shaver.  Granted, that follow-up manual shave went so smoothly, quickly, and painlessly that I could tell the electric had done most of the work, but isn&#x27;t it silly to spend so much time with the electric (almost as much time as a manual), then lather up your face right afterwords and do yet another shave with a manual, thus doubling my shave time?    I really REALLY wish there was a way to make the shave less close.  I know that sounds completely idiotic, but, remember, in my case having a close shave on most of my face but not in random spots looks silly.  I&#x27;d trade that bizarre look in easily for a less close shave that was at least even.  I mean, if I could go from Day5-level stubble back to even Day2 or Day3-level stubble, I&#x27;d go for it (I&#x27;m not in a profession where I need to be cleanly shaven every morning).  Funny thing is that I read online that the U.S. version of this shaver is the old version in parts of Asia (Japan I think?) where the newer version (in black) has three closeness-levels for shaving.  So perhaps if that version ever hits the U.S. market, the level that will leave stubble will allow for a more even shave (if not necessarily perfectly close to the skin).    Okay, on to the pluses (although if you had the experience I had, I&#x27;m sure you&#x27;re regretting buying this).  (1) It&#x27;s a wiz on the upper part of my face (cheeks and mustache), and I literally mean as close as a manual.  Why would I only shave my upper part of my face and not my neck and jawline though is beyond me.  The only upside I suppose is if you prefer the look of stubble everywhere but your mustache -- in which case this is a very expensive but excellent way to get rid of just your mustache hair in a fast, painless process.  (2) It&#x27;s pretty!  I know that sounds stupid, but I like electronics.  This thing is just gorgeous (I got this one, the one with the black-ish sides and back, not the one with the grey sides and back).  It feels good in your hand, beautifully designed on the exterior, and the cleaning system is fun and easy to use.    IN CONCLUSION, this is probably an awesome product for SOME people, depending on your facial hair type.  But I can&#x27;t imagine I&#x27;m the only one who has had this problem of getting a clean shave on top and an awful shave on the neck and jaw, which is why I was surprised I couldn&#x27;t find anyone else saying this in their user reviews before I bought this.  Hopefully this review will at least give you a head&#x27;s up that this is not a one-shaver-fits-all-faces product.</li>

On this and the Series 7, I use the cleaning solution about once a week and then cap the cartridge.  72 db at 6 inches, which makes it less than half as loud as the series 7.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Back to my cost company tonight, I snagged a [[ASIN:B0067D4RYY Philips Norelco 1255x Sensotouch 3d Electric Shaver, Black,Special Value Includes Extra Shaving Head Pack]] apparently a 1250x with the extra head, on sale for one five five with a fifteen mail in rebate.  (I still have my old corded Norelco from decades ago, won&#x27;t do my &#x27;stache correctly, so I have been dubious about these shavers.)  I&#x27;ll be posting my 2 star review tonight; this sucker is going back.  (What a relief to switch back to the Series 5, even if it is slow.)  The only really good thing about the 1255x is the noise: 67 db at 6 inches is about a quarter as loud as the Series 7.  (The decibel scale is logarithmic, not linear.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;------&lt;br /&gt;Update 8-12-2012:  my interpretation of the decibel scale was incorrect.  3db (not 6db) represents a doubling of the sound pressure.  I&#x27;m still using the 5-550cc, which takes at least 50% longer to produce an acceptable shave as my old Series 7.  My credit card provides an extra year of warranty and credited my full Series 7 purchase price to my card, so I&#x27;m probably going to spring for a new Series 7, keep the 5 as a spare.</li>

I also want to point out that the only difference between the Pulsonic 790cc and 760cc is that the 790cc has an lcd screen that shows power level and hygiene level and the 760cc has an led screen where led lights simply light up to indicate battery life.     <li> [[ASIN:B000Q6SU3C Braun Pulsonic System 9595 with LCD Screen]] The package as received was covered with a medium weight smooth plastic cover with no obvious beginning or end. I sat at the table for a while trying to determine how to get a handhold to get it off. Finally, after a while I attacked it with a scissors. What was left was a box with no obvious way to get it open. There did not seem to be a pull-out flap.  I discovered, after time, that it opened like a book with two halves. Inside each half was a part of the product that in some cases had to be wrestled out. No instructions on or in the box that made much sense.  After all this time, I needed a shave. Reading the instruction book and trying to figure out what some of the icons meant I assembled the two parts, cleaner and shaver, finally forced open the container containing the  cleaning fluid and inserted it into the cleaner container. Then charged the battery with the oversized charger (the plug juts about five inches out of the wall.) I waited about 1/2 hour and proceeded to shave. The shave I would rate as very good, once you get used to the excessive vibration. It did all parts of my sorry face without much effort. The cleaner worked well, but P&amp;G devised a very nice cash cow for themselves. The cleaner cartridge, they say should last 30 days at which time buy another one at $3-$4. I find this trend among manufacturers obnoxious. There must be a better way to make the original price the final price. Check other reviews. Consumers are beginning to use their heads.I remove the cartridge during the day and cover it to prevent evaporation and remove the shaver head after shaving to blow out the dust and replace it before putting it in the cleaner.  Finally, in summation, the product is grossly over packaged, very over priced, but does a good job shaving. It is not that portable because you can&#x27;t carry the cleaner with you. You can use water to clean, but then it does not get lubricated by the company&#x27;s cleaner. The plug-charger does not fit into the carrying case provided. Before committing to the \\&quot;Braun\\&quot; check out other shavers and see if they would do a good job for you.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m 27 and I&#x27;ve been using Braun electric shavers almost daily since I started shaving my face, probably about 12 years ago. My face can&#x27;t stand razors either. I wanted to replace my four years old Braun Synchro, not because it was bad, but because I was fooled by advertising, and this shaver looked promising.     Yes, the device looks nice, weighs less than my old Synchro, the movable foils seem a good thing at first, and the cleaning system looks much better (it&#x27;s still quite big, though). But I was hugely disappointed after the first use: my old (and much cheaper) Synchro shaves noticeably closer than this Pulsonic, even though its foil blade should have been replaced by now. The (few) hairs on my neck the Synchro is unable to cut, arent&#x27;t cut by the Pulsonic either. And it gets worse: my skin was much more irritated, especially on my neck, where a lot of red bumps appeared soon after shaving (I used Gillette after shave, as usually). And it happened something that has never happened to me before using an electric razor: the middle foil made a cut in my lower lip (I can&#x27;t do that with my Synchro even if I try to).    Yesterday I gave it another shot but the results were no better than the first time.    The redness and irritation might go away as soon as my face gets used to this shaver, but I doubt it will shave my face any closer in future uses.    I couldn&#x27;t care less about the looks of the shaver, its weight (as long as it&#x27;s reasonable), its battery life (I always use the power cord) or the cleaning system (I use the one that came with my Synchro very few times a year). I just want the closest shave possible without leaving my face tomato-red. And my old Synchro definately does a better job at that than this Pulsonic, so I think I&#x27;ll stick with it.    I really wanted to like this shaver, but I can&#x27;t recommend it. I understand that there are many different types of skin and beard out there, and some guys might get fantastic results with this shaver, as some others do with Philips/Norelco. But check that you can return it if you are going to buy this.</li>

    <li> Braun, a company built on design to solve customer problems, appears to have lost their way with the Pulsonic systems. Until now, I&#x27;ve aways been a fan of their \\&quot;function-dictates-form\\&quot; method, however in this product things went sub-par.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s an okay shave. As with any electric shaver, you have to repeat areas, to get that \\&quot;closer than a blade,\\&quot; look. What gets me is, for $200+, I expect something significantly better from my Braun 5775 and it&#x27;s not. I spend no less time when using the 9595, but there are spots on my face (e.g. under the lower lip, below the cheekbones) that the 5775 seems to pick up faster. While \\&quot;Pulsonic Technology\\&quot; (i.e. faster oscillations) works slightly better in most areas, there are a few areas where it significantly underperforms.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaving cartridge now combines the foil and the cutter, which you can&#x27;t easily clean due to the design. Thus, you need the cleaning system provided by the 9595&#x27;s base. However, you still want to clean the cartridge as the hair, etc. lands in the cleaning fluid. Over time, the pretty blue cleaning fluid becomes a disgusting gray, creating a gooey mass. Is it safe to dump fluid? (I wish Braun had said if it was.) It&#x27;s possible that the faster oscillations required the integration of the cutter and foil, but it&#x27;s also possible Braun wanted to sell an expensive base and the cleaning solution cartridges - now there selling two kinds of \\&quot;blades\\&quot; for their \\&quot;razor.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The base looks nice, however, Braun opted to use the same power plug system they have been using for years. It&#x27;s a black cord with the AC to DC transformer connected to the wall-plug. You&#x27;ve just paid $200+ dollars for a pretty white shaving system and then you have this ugly black cord with a huge transformer sticking out of the wall. For $200+, there could have been a transformer in the base of the 9595 system. On the plus side, when I have to get the spots that my 9595 missed with 5775, I can use the same power cord.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Being a gadget geek, my office with its computers and electronic gear, looks like a swarm of fireflies when I turn off the lights. Personally, I&#x27;d rather it just be dark. I wish electronics vendors would dump the gratuitous LEDs. I am not going to be using the 9595 in the dark, and I do not need a blue LED (on the shaver) and two green LEDs (on the base). The shaver have an LCD display in the base, why have mutiple informational interfaces?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, why, after paying a ransom, does this shaver not have a replaceable battery? Lithium-ion batteries will wear out after a few years. The marketing copy on the cartridges which claims the system is like new when you replace the cleaning cartridge is overlooking the expensive cutter/foil $36, the cleaning cartridges 2 for $10 and, finally, the battery.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Adding insult to injury, after a year without replacing the cartridge, the base would no longer do the brief \\&quot;econo clean.\\&quot; It was as if the system was passively aggressively insisting I replace the cartridge. And, after replacing the cartridge, the system again would do the \\&quot;econo clean.\\&quot; That&#x27;s not a feature, that&#x27;s a nuisance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Since my 5775 was a quarter the cost of the 9595 and that the Braun brand is a strong one, I expected more. It&#x27;s a good shaver, but the value this shaver gives is not worth the cost. I fear I fell into the hype of \\&quot;Pulsonic Technology.\\&quot;y office with its computers and electronic gear, looks like a swarm of fireflies when I turn off the lights. Personally, I&#x27;d rather it just be dark. I wish electronics vendors would dump the gratuitous LEDs. I am not going to be using the 9595 in the dark, and I do not need a blue LED (on the shaver) and two green LEDs (on the base). The shaver have an LCD display in the base, why have mutiple informational interfaces?     Finally, why, after paying a ransom, does this shaver not have a replaceable battery? Lithium-ion batteries will wear out after a few years. The marketing copy on the cartridges which claims the system is like new when you replace the cleaning cartridge is overlooking the expensive cutter/foil $36, the cleaning cartridges 2 for $10 and, finally, the battery.    Adding insult to injury, after a year without replacing the cartridge, the base would no longer do the brief \\&quot;econo clean.\\&quot; It was as if the system was passively aggressively insisting I replace the cartridge. And, after replacing the cartridge, the system again would do the \\&quot;econo clean.\\&quot; That&#x27;s not a feature, that&#x27;s a nuisance.      Since my 5775 was a quarter the cost of the 9595 and that the Braun brand is a strong one, I expected more. It&#x27;s a good shaver, but the value this shaver gives is not worth the cost. I fear I fell into the hype of \\&quot;Pulsonic Technology.\\&quot;</li>

    <li> The pressure facing health and beauty grooming appliances is tough... they have to constantly think of new and better ways to improve their products, EVEN THOUGH they may have already reached a technological ceiling. It&#x27;s because of the competitive nature of the business. They could make subtle improvements in an existing shaver and price it less, but people won&#x27;t buy it because there isn&#x27;t some compelling difference. So, companies keep trying to invent catch phrases and ambiguous functionality, in order to keep prices up (with the illusion that you&#x27;re getting more if you pay more).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;How much better can a foil shaver get? Braun reached a major pinnacle with the 7000 series. The Syncro line was the first introducing a head cleaning system, as well as a faster motor with side-to-side vibration. You take a shave with a 7000 series and this new 7 series, and guess what? You won&#x27;t feel a noticeable difference. A few other reviewers have noticed this as well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Having been a Braun shaver owner for over 15 years, my latest model is the 8595 Activator. It is the equivalent to the 9595, only being from the previous generation. It has almost everything the 9595 has, except for the new casing design and the indicator that tells you when to change the shaving head cassette.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I happened to have a friend who bought one of these and managed to get him to loan it to me for a week (we traded shavers). Guess what? After a week, we compared notes and discovered that we BOTH found the shaving performance identical between the 8595 Activator and the 790cc Pulsonic (9595).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Braun lauds its \\&quot;new\\&quot; Pulsonic technology, but in essence it is the same technology they&#x27;ve had since the 7000 series. Quite frankly, I don&#x27;t think it&#x27;s worth spending an extra $100 to get the Series 7 model. Instead, I&#x27;d buy a new old stock 8595 or 8995 model for about $100 cheaper. Also, you&#x27;ll save quite a bit of money of the long haul on head replacements. The 9595 (790) uses a \\&quot;cassette\\&quot;, which is essentially the foil and cutter block combined into one unit. You cannot buy them separately. You damage the foil? The whole thing requires replacing. Why did Braun do this? Well... to close a loop hole. On the earlier models, you can replace just the cutter block and keep the your current foil. After all, if the foil is undamaged, it is still doing its job. From a shaving outlet, you can buy the 8000 series cutter block for just $10. The 9595 cassette costs $50! You do the math...lly the foil and cutter block combined into one unit. You cannot buy them separately. You damage the foil? The whole thing requires replacing. Why did Braun do this? Well... to close a loop hole. On the earlier models, you can replace just the cutter block and keep the your current foil. After all, if the foil is undamaged, it is still doing its job. From a shaving outlet, you can buy the 8000 series cutter block for just $10. The 9595 cassette costs $50! You do the math...</li>
    <li> My results with the Pulsonic are not baby&#x27;s butt smooth across my bread. However, I&#x27;ve tried everything available except a straight razor, and nothing gets there. There are always areas where rubbing against the grain will detect minute stubble. Even with an aggressive razor (Merkur Slant Bar with Feather blades) and aggressive techniques (blade buffing and j-hooking), that stubble can not be removed without cuts or razor burn. The Pulsonic is a significant improvement over previous Braun shavers. I can get the same results in 2 minutes with the Pulsonic compared to 15 minutes with a wet shave. That wins my vote.</li>

    <li> I have had a Braun electric razor for several years. After buying new blades but still not getting the shave I wanted, I decided the buy a new razor with the cleaning system.     <li> I&#x27;ve stepped to electric razors a couple years ago.  Previously I used both the leading Gillette Fusion and Shick Quattro razors.  I stepped to electric razors as an attempt to reduce cutting irritation and provide a quicker, less fuss shave.    My first step was to a Braun Series 1 as a trial.  It had good reviews as a budget razor.  Initial impressions were mediocre.  The big issue was I don&#x27;t shave daily all the time, and once the hairs get long, foil razors stop being efficient.  Shave time goes way up.  I basically said screw it and went towards the high end.  I wanted to see if the best available could give me what I wanted.    I first started with Norelco&#x27;s SmartTouch XL razor because the rotary type razors function better with longer hairs.  I got it just before the Arcitec came out and represented the best Norelco product available at the time.  I was also considering the Braun Pulsonic as an option, but the price difference wasn&#x27;t worth it at the time.    The SmartTouch is an excellent razor.  The 3 layer cutting and circular design works outstanding for getting most of the hairs quickly and easily.  The rotary type razors are quiet and fast working on even very long hairs.  The relatively slow rpm does limit overall cutting rate on really long and thick hair.  Pull is minimum, but you can tell there&#x27;s a little wait time if you try and cut fast.  The only real downside of this type of razor is that it doesn&#x27;t cut as close to the skin as a foil type razor.  It ends up taking a significant amount of pressure against the skin to get the razor to cut really close like a razor.  To do so, you will need some sort of lubricant, but soap and water does work fine.  There&#x27;s just a bit of friction from the shaver.  Really close shaves can rash the skin a little bit if you try too hard.    I stepped to the Braun Pulsonic as a trial to see if I could do better than the Norelco product.  I found one for a good price eventually and grabbed it.  The big thing I liked about the Pulsonic that made it different from other foil razors was that it had the center long hair cutter.  This was a big deal because long hairs is the greatest enemy of foil type cutters.  It&#x27;s great to see Braun also adding this to lower level razors now because it works great.  There are several things I like about the Braun razor over the Norelco.  First, it cuts faster.  You can not shave for a week and even though it&#x27;s a foil shaver, it will cut off a lot of it very quickly due to that center long hair cutter.  Once a lot of the long hairs are cut down, the foil cutters work the rest down quickly.  Shave speed gains might be around 20%.  Plus the shave gets closer than the Norelco with less pressure.  It&#x27;s much easier to get a razor close shave with the Pulsonic.  The razor also glides over the skin quite easily.  Even if you put a bit of pressure against the skin, the Braun glides over the skin well.  The braun doesn&#x27;t really rash the skin much even with pressed moderately to the skin.  The Braun can chop a little bit at the skin though (not painful/deep, but little one layer cuts here and there).      Now there are some traits I do not like.  The Braun razor is significantly louder, just a lot more noisy.  Rotary razors are just really quiet.  Foil razors have the loud buzz you common think of and the Pulsonic is no exception.  The foil type razor is also sensitive to cutting direction.  With the areas where the hairs like to lay down, the Braun has trouble grabbing and cutting these hairs.  You have to make sure you go against the lay and you typically have to brush your hand against the lay to raise them up before you go over them with the razor.  Wipe across the stubborn hairs with a hand, and zip over them with the razor.  This works slick and pretty easily counters the troublesome hairs.  Since rotary razors like the Norelco cut in all directions and that you typically use them in a circular manner, they tend to get those stubborn hairs a little easier.    Some notes on long term wear.  I used each for a little over a year.  The Norelco experienced little to no wear.  I never replaced the cutters and I got the unit used.  It worked as good as new the day I stopped using it.  The unit was sold to me at a pretty cheap price due to the cleaning base being broken.  It wasn&#x27;t actually broken, just stuck and was oddly jammed.  I quickly popped it free, and it worked great.  The Norelco showed no wear after a year of use and looks and functions just like new.  A roommate of mine is now using it and enjoys it.    I got the Braun shaver used as well, used for a few months I believe.  I got some fresh cleaner for the base but never touched the cutter during my use.  The Braun has functioned well for the year, but a couple little problems have popped up.  First, there is some flaking of the painted surface near the cutter.  I assumed the cleaning solution does slightly break down the paint over time.  It doesn&#x27;t seem to wear at all by handling though, so the paint is durable to the hand.  It just seems to be the cleaning solution doing it.  Second, the charging base has two spring loaded tabs that the charging pins on the razor sit against to charge.  These tabs are a painted plastic, and the paint is conductive enough to transfer electricity.  Well, one of the tabs now has the paint flaking off, so now the razor has trouble charging or cleaning.  This needs to be fixed using some sort of conductive paint or something.  The razor can be plugged in directly to the cord, but it sort of makes the cleaning base useless.  The cleaning base does function and last well otherwise.  The cleaning solution even lasts quite a long time as you don&#x27;t use it all the time.  Clean it once a week or two and wash after normal use, the solution easily lasts a year which was surprising.  I am finally replacing the cutter head on the braunt.  The 18 month suggestion seems decently accurate for wear.  It starts to cut a little slower (not much) and starts to pull just a little bit.  Connection points within the razor are plastic, so I assume there is some wear over time too that may limit vibration intensity.  There really isn&#x27;t visual wear, so design and materials seem proper.  Other than some minor wear issues, the razor has held up well.    So, is the Braun Pulsonic the best razor I&#x27;ve used?  Yes.  I can say that I do consider it a better razor.  It shaves faster and shaves closer than the Norelco product.  Its use however is a little more tricky.  It takes a little more skill and understanding to shave your face quickly and to get all the stubborn hairs.  The Norelco is a better no fuss razor.  You just go around your face until everything&#x27;s cut.  It&#x27;s just as quick or as close without significant skin pressure (requiring some lubrication to do).    What about hand razors again?  Well, going back, I do find both the Fusion and Quattro both harsher on the skin.  The Fusion is great about getting a really close shave and go through long, thick hair without clogging, but it pulls a lot.  The cut is just very sharp.  The Quattro is much smoother in its cutting, and I tended to prefer it.  It does clog easily though when going through a lot of hair and deep hair.  Both wear very slowly.  The titanium bladed Quattro takes forever to wear down.  I still use a hand razor for some minor trimming here and there, but have pretty much exclusively used electric razors for the last couple years.  Time wise, hand razors can be quicker in some cases, but both approaches do take a similar amount of time.  Electric can be faster if you don&#x27;t care about the random stubborn hairs or don&#x27;t care about a razor close shave.  If you use an electric maybe twice a day, you could zip through the process in a minute.  If you don&#x27;t shave for several days, and want a no hair, razor close shave, it could take about 5-6 minutes.</li>
    <li> This shaver does a great job. It is clean, efficient, overall I give the shaver itself a 5 star.    However, once you use the shaver, you have to put it back into a plastic cleaning dock that cleans the shaving heads and recharges the battery.     The fit of the shaver into the dock is so inadequate that the blue led on the shaver (the one that shows it is charging) sometimes flashes intermittently. (the dock does fantastic light shows while this happens...) You start the cleaning cycle and the shaver vibrates away from the charging contacts. So the cleaning cycle stops. I look forward to shaving now.  I&#x27;m not regretting the change.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;Close shave, as close as you want it.  Spend enough time on it and you will have a baby smooth shave.&lt;br /&gt;Auto-clean with lemon scent.&lt;br /&gt;No more opening the top and shaking it over the toilet or garbage can to dump clippings.&lt;br /&gt;Rock solid construction.  It&#x27;s metal and heavy with a rubber back for grip.  Very well made by samurais in germany.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;Expensive.&lt;br /&gt;You need to go over neck areas against the grain of your beard a lot to get a close shave there, much more so than my last rotary shaver.  But once achieved, the closeness is better than a rotary provides.&lt;br /&gt;Louder than a rotary.  Bzzzzzzzz.&lt;br /&gt;Buying replacement cleaning solution.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I see the price went way up after I bought it.  I bought it for $189, looks like it is for sale on Amazon for $250+ now following the same link I purchased it from.  What&#x27;s that all about?  Not sure I would pay that.  For under $200, buy it.  Every other good electric shaver is $140 and up anyway.  Good luck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Edit 2012:  Some of the silver coating on the back of the razor near the head piece has bubbled and peeled away and it is black underneath.  This was most likely caused by the cleaning solution.  Apparently it is coated with a paint that reacts to the cleaning solution.  I peeled it away with my fingernail.The razor is less attractive now, but still functions very well.  The total area of the peeling is about 1/8th of an inch tall and across the entire back.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Edit 2014: My old Braun continues to function flawlessly.  I have had no new paint loss after the initial problem and the cleaning station looks and functions as good as the day it was new.  Not sure what the Braun company is making now (obviously not the model I bought), but if they still make the same quality products they made when I bought mine, then buy with confidence.  I have had no battery issues or performance issues.  It charges and cleans like new after all these years. I replaced the foil once a while ago and that was the only maintenance.  Money very well spent.</li>

I read every review I could find on this unit to be absolutely sure that this one was going to be the answer to my dreams for a easy, quick, close shave.    Well, after a week of hemming and hawing, I bought it.  It was here in 3 days and I charged her up.  The next morning, I gave the Braun 790 a spin for the first time.  I did it as recommended, prior to washing face and showering.  I tried that once with the Norelco and I ended up having to shower and shave again, just to make it look as if I shaved that morning.    For me this 790 gave me the closest shave I have ever experienced using an electric razor in all of my shaving years. When I was finished, my face felt like \\&quot;Monday morning blade smooth\\&quot;. No irritation at all, and SUPER close.  I have been using the Braun 790 for close to 4 weeks now and have never gone back to blade.  There is no need to. The Braun removed that pain from my life!  Bye-bye shaving cream.  I love the automatic cleaning process.  Just set the shaver in the base. The base chooses the correct cleaning cycle based on use and then the next morning I have clean, lemony fresh and oiled shaver ready to go.  Always out of box clean.  And the lithium battery, of which I have always wished for has no memory, so I do not have to run the razor from top to bottom charge anymore.  Just charge it everyday while it is cleaning.  NO problem!  Thank you Braun.  I have never spent over $200 for an electric razor, but it is comforting to know that Braun has created the electric razor that I will use for the rest of my living years. WORTH EVERY PENNEY!  Including the future purchases for cleaning solution.  WORTH EVERY PENNY!  This is the razor that my father had always dreamed of having.  I only wish he could have experienced what I am experiencing these last 4 weeks and for the rest of my life.</li>

Must have been because of the Panasonic I had before and the fact that I could only get decent results by mashing it hard against my skin. I now have learned to let it glide across my flesh and get even better and faster results.    In regards to the cleaning solution. As I&#x27;ve already mentioned- I only need to shave once every other day and that is the regiment that I follow. I do use the cleaning base after every shave. It has now been roughly 6 weeks since I&#x27;ve owned the shaver and my read out on the display base still shows my fluid level at \\&quot;HIGH\\&quot;. So, again this may be dependent on the person and how much stubble thye&#x27;ve collected. One thing I do after every other shave is just remove the foil and tap out the stubble into the sink. Not sure if this has any effect but, that&#x27;s what I do. When I pop the shaver into the base after each shave and allow it to auto select the cleaning that the razor needs it has always selected \\&quot;ECO\\&quot; mode. As another experiment on one occassion I did not clean it until after 2 shaves. When I popped it into the base auto select went to \\&quot;NORMAL\\&quot; mode. So i beleive it is all working correctly.    On a side note to that- you can get the cleaning cartridges here on Amazon in either 2 or 3 packs. Pay close attention to the pricing on them. Sometimes it is only a dollar or 2 more to get 2- 2 packs (total of 4 cartridges) then it is to get 1- 3 pack. And other times it&#x27;s cheaper to get 1- 3 pack vs. 2-2 packs.</li>

    <li> I purchased this shaver several months ago, and decided to provide my review after using it almost daily during that period.  This is a lengthy review.    History  I&#x27;ve been a manual razor user since I began shaving, but I did dabble in various electric razors.  I received an expensive rotary electric razor as a gift but found it missed too many hairs, eventually returning to a manual razor.  During my Army days, I purchased a cheap (under twenty dollars) foil razor, which worked surprisingly well during those field training exercises when I didn&#x27;t bring my usual manual razor.  I learned that the foil razors shaved my face better than the rotary version; this experience influenced my decision to later buy this foil razor.  So, many years went by, but I still favored my manual (multi-blade) razor with grocery store shaving cream.  I developed an interest in wet shaving using the old-fashioned double-edge (DE) safety razors, with a high-quality shaving cream and badger brush.  Although it&#x27;s more time consuming, DE shaving is my favorite; it provides me with the absolute closest shave possible.  Unfortunately, I developed a skin condition on my face called rosacea, which is basically a red, painful swelling, which can be aggravated by daily shaving with a blade.  I visited my physician, who not only prescribed a gel called Metrogel but also recommended I switch to an electric razor.  He warned me that many guys accustomed to shaving with a manual razor, may be disappointed with electric razors since they don&#x27;t shave as close as a blade.    Experience  I know I want a foil (versus rotary) shaver because of my prior experience.  Since the new shaver would become my primary tool, I want a high quality item that provides the closest shave an electric razor can provide.  After a much searching, I settled on the Braun brand, and after more research, settled on their top-of-line model, 790cc.  Here&#x27;s what I like, in no particular order:    1.  Heavy (but not too heavy).  It feels good in the hand.  2.  Powerful.  It cuts through whiskers (even several days&#x27; worth of growth) without hesitation.  3.  No pinching.  I find that cheaper razors can cause razor burn or painful pinching.  4.  Cleaning options.  Basically, there are a couple of ways to do this.  One is to use the included base station.  Drop the unit in, and press the button.  It cleans and recharges the razor and comes out smelling \\&quot;lemony\\&quot; afterwards.  Some reviewers feel this is a scam by Braun to generate more revenue by selling refills for the base station.  My experience is that refills are required about every 5 weeks or so with daily use.  Replacements are about six dollars, and I don&#x27;t mind paying for the convenience.  However, the directions state that the razor can be cleaned by running under water and periodically putting a little machine oil on the cutting block.  5.  Travels well.  I use this on short trips (&lt; 5 days).  Fully charged, the unit lasts approximately for 5 days.  If necessary, the power cord can be detached from the base station and taken for longer trips.  If the unit is no longer charged, it can be used with the power cord plugged in.  The travel case is sturdy and holds up fine in my carry on (by the way, I&#x27;ve had no trouble taking this unit through airport security check points (just to be clear, I never take the base station with me, but leave that at home).  6.  It doesn&#x27;t heat up.  Cheaper razors tend to get quite warm after being on for a while.  This doesn&#x27;t do that.  7.  Side-burn trimmer.  OK, this is not great, but it&#x27;s pretty good.  Sometime I&#x27;ll whip out my DE razor to get a perfect side-burn trim.  8.  Battery/Hygiene indicator.  The battery indicator is nice to have, especially when traveling.  The hygiene indicator is interesting, but I just drop the unit the base station after each use and clean it, so I don&#x27;t pay much attention to that piece of it.  9.  Shave quality.  I saved this for last.  The shave quality is phenomenal, but it doesn&#x27;t start off that way.  It takes time (a couple of weeks) for the face to become accustomed to the razor.  The shave will improve as (1) your face adjusts, and (2) your technique improves.  Technique is really a function of the way you adjust to the many directions of whisker growth.  Be sure to shave against the grain.  Also, if you&#x27;re moving from a manual razor to this one, do not alternate during this transition period.  You&#x27;ll just prolong the adjustment period.  This razor it not designed to be use on a wet face.  Face should be clean and dry.  I usually wash my face, dry it throughly, and apply an electric pre-shave solution.  Although an electric pre-shave solution is not required, I find that it helps immensely in getting a really close shave (virtually as close as a manual razor).  Although this is a little off topic, I will emphasize that a pre-shave solution helps tremendously.  My favorite is Lab Series (unscented), while my second favorite is Anthony (lightly scented).  I&#x27;ve used Williams Lectric Shave, and although it works great, the smell is too strong for me.    A couple more points  1.  Some people recommend refilling the cleaning solution holder with rubbing alcohol, in an attempt to save money.  These aren&#x27;t designed to be refilled.  More importantly, the cleaning solution appears to contain some sort of lubricant (in addition to alcohol and a lemon scent).  This is obvious if you dip your finger in the solution and rub your fingers together.  If you&#x27;re going to spend two hundred or more dollars on this razor, follow the directions and either (1) use the base station with appropriate cleaning solution refills, or (2) don&#x27;t use the base station and instead rinse the unit per the instructions.  2.   As your face adjusts and your technique improves, you&#x27;ll notice your shaves improving to a point where they&#x27;re almost as close as a manual razor.  It took me several months to realize the importance of using a good electric pre-shave solution.    Summary  Although it&#x27;s expensive, it&#x27;s a wonderful product.  My rosacea is under control, my shaves are close (almost as close as a blade), and it takes me significantly less time to shave in the morning.  My shaves are close enough that I don&#x27;t need to do any touch-up shaving later in the day.  I highly recommend.</li>

I think the pulsing effect actually gets the blood flow moving in your face and helps to tone (my perception, not scientifically proven).     <li> This review is based entirely upon my initial impressions as I have only used the razor a few times.  I will update the review as needed with further use of the product.  For readability, i&#x27;ve broken the review into several sections:    Design - of course the design matters, it&#x27;s the first thing that you see and determines how the razor will interact with your face.  With a blue and silver exterior, the razor sure looks fancy.  To match its external prowess, the razor utilizes a tilting head to completely shave your face - this works great.  This model also comes with a handy locking mechanism for the head to reach hard to get areas on your face - also works great. Overall design:  A+    Comfort - the comfort of the shave is great, no burning, no pulling, and a very minimal amount of irritation.  Overall comfort:  A+    Noise/Heat - This is my biggest complaint with the razor so far - it&#x27;s fairly loud (at least compared to Norelco rotary razors i&#x27;ve used in the past).  Also, there seems to be a fair amount of heat radiated (not uncomfortable at all though) by the foil unit - this is only noticeable when using the lock on the tilting function.  Overall noise:  B    Performance - This is of course the most important part of the shaver - will it at the end of day adequately shave your face?  With no reservations, I can say that this razor does a fabulous job of shaving one&#x27;s face.  It misses very little hair and thus requires a minimal amount of rehasing on your face.  Much better over Norelco rotaries (esp the wet shave system) and comparable (but not quite as good) to an \\&quot;old fashioned\\&quot; blade.  Performance:  A+    Cleaning and Charging System:  The razor seems to charge fairly quickly, with the ability for a quick charge or to plug the AC adapter directly into the razor.  The cleaning system seems adequate - Braun suggests to clean the razor after every use, I don&#x27;t think this is necessary and will probably only clean every several uses as the Clean and Renew solution is an added cost (~ $4 a cartridge).  You can also clean the razor the old fashion way with water and remove the cartridge head - but the clean and renew system seems so much better.  The only downside is the engineering of the clean and renew cartridges - you open them and they almost immediately spill a little.  I would like to have seen an elevated spout for opening to avoid this problem.  Overall cleaning and charging:  A    Overall comments - If your sick of the lack of quality from comparably priced rotary shavers and/or don&#x27;t like the cuts, roughness, and cost of a shave from a blade, then this razor is certainly a good candidate for you.  As far as cost is concerned, it doesn&#x27;t seem too bad, though there is a large initial investment in the razor (NOTE:  amazon often offers 50 dollars off a future order with a purchase of at least $139 in products from Braun/Oral-B).  In addition, there is a small amount of maintenance costs in the form of replacing the cartridge/foil unit  (about $30 - Braun recommends this be done once a year) and refilling the clean and renew system (about $4/ea from amazon in the 3 pack) where the latter is highly dependent on how much you personally clean the razor and your use of water instead of the clean and renew system.  Overall, this is the best razor i&#x27;ve ever used and don&#x27;t regret the purchase at all!  Overall grade - A    P.S.  - For those of that are still worried about Amazon&#x27;s no-return policy on this item, Braun offers a 60 day money back gurantee in the US.</li>

Much to my suprise, my first shave was as close as I&#x27;ve ever gotten with a razor, twice as fast, and left no irritation,no in grown hairs, no break outs, and no redness.  Not only that, but the miniscule amount of hair in the sink makes my girfriend think I take the time to clean up after every shave even when I&#x27;m in a hurry!  I can&#x27;t say enough about this razor, and while I don&#x27;t have much to compare it to, simply knowing it has done its job for a month straight with no issues, and hasn&#x27;t seemed to dull at all, astounds me.     I can&#x27;t think of the last thing I bought that was this useful, and that I&#x27;m as appreciative for each time I use it.  Can I say more than I would shave MAYBE once a year with a razor and since the day I bought it I&#x27;ve shaved every morning with the Braun?!    Granted, it still won&#x27;t get every hair on your neck, but it does an amazingly good job of skimming over any ingrown hairs so you can pluck them out later, and not grabbing or yanking hairs that are slightly longer than the rest.    Nothing but 5 stars from me.</li>

I also think the charge doesn&#x27;t last as long as other shavers I&#x27;ve owned.    In my opinion the razor is made from cheap material.  An example is when pushing the button to release the head mine clicks really hard like its breaking.  I&#x27;ve noticed that only one side releases unless my finger is centered precisely on the button.  Shouldn&#x27;t be happening with something this expensive.  Second example is my lock button broke last week.  I can no longer lock the head.  It wasn&#x27;t comforting to hear the guy at the Service Center say \\&quot;Wow, haven&#x27;t heard of that happening before, I&#x27;m not sure how to fix it, guess I&#x27;ll have to order a head from the company.\\&quot;  Then he asked \\&quot;do you have another razor?  It&#x27;ll take 10-15 days to get the part from the company.\\&quot;  I&#x27;m heading overseas in a couple of weeks, I don&#x27;t think this razor is making the trip.  Its pretty though, anyone that uses my bathroom usually comes out saying \\&quot;dang man that razor is awesome.\\&quot;  If they only knew.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve used Norelco shavers for forty years, but based on other reviews I&#x27;ve read I decided to give the Pulsonic a try.  The vibration takes some getting used to (one wonders if they didn&#x27;t start calling the problem of high noise levels a feature), but it does shave extremely close--close enough that I get razor burn that I never had with my Norelco.      Another noticeable thing is that the screens get quite warm during operation.  Don&#x27;t know if this will reduce as the screens and cutters wear in (I&#x27;ve only had mine a month) or not.  I did find that I had to change my shaving pattern to a more linear one than I was used to, since the Norelco cuts equally well in any direction, but having done so, the Pulsonic&#x27;s pivoting head tracks the shape of my face very well.      I also found that I had to change the way I shaved around the corners of my mouth and under my nose.  Norelcos cut right up to the edge of their heads, but there is a big dead zone at the ends of the Braun&#x27;s heads that doesn&#x27;t cut.  As a result, you can&#x27;t use the corner of the head to shave into the opening of your nostrils or the ends of your mouth; you have to use the middle of the head, which is less convenient.    The Pulsonic cleaning system is handy, although it takes up a lot of room on the counter, and there&#x27;s the extra cost of buying cleaning cartridges. It&#x27;s probably worth it, however, for people who never remember to clean their shaver.     Finally, this was the most over packaged product I have ever seen, with a molded plastic shell (inside a cardboard box, which was inside a cardboard sleeve, which was inside a plastic box) held together by little buttons that were so confusing they had to put an instruction sticker in the box describing how to get it open.  Some German engineer got entirely too carried away with the package design, which probably contributed to the unit&#x27;s high price.</li>

It continues to give the closes shaves of my life.  I ultimately began changing the shaving blocks once each year.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I noticed about 18 months ago that the red light indicating the status of the cleaning/lubricating fluid began to come on too soon.  I finally put the recharger/cradle under the faucet and washed out the insides very thoroughly.  I found a lot of hair shavings had clogged-up the workings which caused it to give premature readings.  It worked like new once I had done this.  I recommend you do the same every year, and you save on cleaning/lubricating fluid.he blades will be sanitized, lubricated and ready for the next morning&#x27;s session with a minimum of effort and thought on my part. It also has a 25-second quick cleaning cycle for when you have to use your shaver in a hurry (This feature is only available on the Braun Pulsonic System 9595CC with LCD Screen, not on the lesser equipped Braun Pulsonic System 9585CC with LED Lights). After each cleaning, the shaver smells clean and lemony.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver can be washed under tap water but with this method of cleaning, the manual states that the shaver head needs to be lubed with a few drops of lubricant every week or so.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shaver sports an LCD screen which has a \\&quot;hygiene\\&quot; and a \\&quot;battery\\&quot; indicator each of which has six graduations/levels arranged in a semi-circular fashion and occupies half of the screen. The hygiene indicator shows when the shaver needs to be cleaned. The battery indicator, of course, indicates how much power is left.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;No time to wait around for the shaver to recharge? No problem. The power cord can be hooked up directly to the shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; Warranty&lt;br /&gt;The shaver has a 2-year warranty (excludes the Cutter and Foil part - you&#x27;re advised to replace this every 18 months).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; Ergonomics&lt;br /&gt;The back and sides of the shaver are rubberized to help you to maintain a firm and comfortable grip while shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; Aesthetics&lt;br /&gt;The Braun Pulsonic System 9595CC exudes elegance, class and sophistication with its sleek lines and its beautifully crafted elements that convey a work of intricate and robust engineering.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;** Cons **&lt;br /&gt;I have only one. Here it is for completeness sake:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; Price&lt;br /&gt;The real gripe I have about this shaver is not so much its price because it&#x27;s a one-time expense but the price of the Clean &amp; Renew cartridges. Talk about \\&quot;giving away razors to sell razor blades\\&quot; except in this case the razor is, patently, not free. Braun advises that the cartridge be replaced after 30 cleaning cycles or 6-8 weeks WCF.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;** Additional Points **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&gt;&gt; Economic Considerations&lt;br /&gt;Some economically-conscious people have suggested using isopropyl alcohol mixed with a lubricant to refill the cartridge. The factory cleaning fluid actually contains a highly volatile alcohol and a lubricant component, which is apparent after each cleaning because the residual lubricant can be felt if you run your finger through the sides of the shaver head. They further suggest removing the cartridge and capping it after each cleaning to prevent the loss of the highly volatile fluid. That&#x27;s too much of a hassle and I don&#x27;t see it as a necessity because once the cartridge is in place, the openings of the cartridge form a watertight seal with the cleaning component and the loss of the solution through evaporation is very minimal. At least one individual suggested changing the cartridge every 6-months.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;** Conclusion **&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Braun Pulsonic System 9595CC with LCD is pricey but it is worth every penny. Don&#x27;t let the price of the Clean &amp; Renew cartridges deter you from getting this little gem because you can always forego the automated cleaning option and simply use running tap water. I personally have no regrets about getting this shaver and I highly recommend it. Go on, get it and see for yourself how the Braun Pulsonic System 9595CC with LCD lives up to its hype.enings of the cartridge form a watertight seal with the cleaning component and the loss of the solution through evaporation is very minimal. At least one individual suggested changing the cartridge every 6-months.      ** Conclusion **    The Braun Pulsonic System 9595CC with LCD is pricey but it is worth every penny. Don&#x27;t let the price of the Clean &amp; Renew cartridges deter you from getting this little gem because you can always forego the automated cleaning option and simply use running tap water.     <li> I have a very heavy and fast growing beard while also having a very sensitive neck and under-lip area, so I am always on a quest for a razor that can somehow cut down my crazy facial hair and not leave me with horrible razor burn.    My first razor was a norelco rotary which is actually quite good at cutting very long hairs but not at getting a close shave, particularly around the chin and neck.    The second was one of the first generation Braun synchro shavers with the cleaning system.  I found that foil shavers, at least on my face, did a much better job getting in close than the rotary shavers.  However this razor was not as good at cutting longer hairs or my neck area.    I have also used a Mach 3 and the Fusion wet razors.  These give the closest shave but leave me with razor burn the next day that is just brutal to re-shave.  That and when you nick yourself with the fusion you end up with 5 little cuts all bleeding, not so much fun.  Also the cost of the cartridges and shaving creams add up very quickly when I am lucky to get a week out of a single blade cartridge.    Finally, we come to the Pulsonic.  This is an electric shaver that actually leaves my face and neck smooth in every area, yet does not leave me with horrible razor burn.  The head glides over my face easily and does not pull or tug or get horribly warm.  For those areas where the head moves too easily, the lock switch will fix the head into position allowing for precision control.  There is of course a pop-up trimmer for getting long hairs down to size.    The cleaning base on this model is MUCH improved over the original synchro, which had an arm that had to be pushed into the back of the razor (this eventually failed, making the base useless).  Instead this one just has two metal contacts that the razor rests against for charging.  No moving parts.  Cleaning is quick and efficient due to the more intelligent cleaning system that will do light cleanings when the razor has not been used as much.Also, this base uses gentle heating to dry the razor instead of a noisy fan like the old models.    The plastic carrying case is very nice as it will keep the razor safe from crushing while in your luggage and it holds the brush for cleaning while traveling (the head is also washable).  While some complain that it does not hold the charger, this is a moot point to me as the charger just goes in with other electronic chargers or in my toiletry bag.    All in all, I am extremely impressed with this razor.  It seems to fix the design flaws with the original synchro models as well as greatly improving shaving performance.  While the price is steep, finally getting a close shave while not suffering from razor burn makes it worth every penny.  It looks like my quest for a razor that can give me near wet razor closeness without the irritation is finally finished.</li>

I assume this is do to the fact that it&#x27;s not as flat and regular there, as well as the fact that the hairs grow multiple directions there.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now I have used it for almost a month.  I am very happy with the ease of use, and the self cleaning system.  On the upper part of my face it still does very well and cuts very close.  On the lower part it is getting more and more on the first pass.  Also, it is leaving less and less completely missed hairs, and sometimes even gets them eventually with multiple passes.  I really feel that eventually I will not have to take out my blade at all to catch these misses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall I am very pleased with this razor.  I don&#x27;t give it 5 stars due to the fact that I still have to use my blade on my neck on occasion.  I can say that I haven&#x27;t found an electric razor that does better than this one yet.eventually I will not have to take out my blade at all to catch these misses.    Overall I am very pleased with this razor.  I don&#x27;t give it 5 stars due to the fact that I still have to use my blade on my neck on occasion.
