    <li> I bought the first \\&quot;self-cleaning\\&quot; Braun shaver when it hit the market back in 2000.  It was the Braun Syncro 7570.  I loved that shaver - easily the best I&#x27;d ever used in my life.  It lasted almost 10 years before the trimmer finally got jammed and I had to replace it.  I had all those spare, blue \\&quot;Clean &amp; Renew\\&quot; cartridges lying around, so of course I was going to buy another Braun.    I&#x27;ve been using the Series 7 - 790cc model for about a month now.  It&#x27;s not bad.  It does give a very close shave.  I can see four big downgrades from the Syncro model though:    1) This new Braun hurts my neck hair when I first start shaving - it feels like it&#x27;s yanking my hair like an Epilady womens&#x27; razor or something.    2) The battery life meter on the old Syncro 7570 told me exactly how many minutes of battery life I had remaining so I could manage my last shave accordingly (move faster or slower to finish the shave just as the battery was dying).  This new model just shows 6 battery-life boxes.  If you&#x27;re on the last box, that could mean anywhere from 1-10 minutes remaning.  I dunno.    3) The little pop out trimmer on this Braun sticks out at an odd 90-degree angle.  The old Syncro trimmer stuck out stright-up, parallel with the shaver.  I have a hard time trimming my own neck hair in the back with this new design because it&#x27;s much harder to see over the bulky head of the shaver.    4) Every time I want to clean the 790cc using the base and the cleaning solution, I have to charge the shaver at the same time.  I don&#x27;t like charging batteries until they are completely dead.  The old Syncro gave me the option to clean and/or charge.  This new model just gives you different cleaning settings, but as far as I can tell, they all charge the unit at the same time.  Big design flaw, in my opinion.    So, in conclusion, the Braun shavers are still the best.  I think this newest model gives the closest shave yet.  But given the 4 issues I listed above, I have to give this shaver 4 outof 5 stars.  The old Braun Syncro model was still the king.  That one gets 5-of-5 stars from me.</li>

    <li> Let me preface this review by stating that I am a loyal Braun fan and customer and have been for nearly twenty years. This electric razor is my fourth Braun in two decades of shaving with nothing else.    This shaver was a \\&quot;To:Me, From:Me\\&quot; gift meant to replace my old Braun, the former TOL Activator Series. The old shaver still did a good job, but after five years , the battery life was markedly less than previous years and the clean &amp; renew base charger unit needed to be replaced due to a broken latch (common repair complaint). Instead of getting the shaver re-fitted with a new battery and replacing the broken base charger, I figured I&#x27;d put that money towards the new \\&quot;upgraded\\&quot; TOL Pulsonic Model 790 instead. The Amazon \\&quot;rebate\\&quot;, as well as double-triple points on the new Amazon/Chase Visa made the choice a no-brainer, or so I thought.    I must say that, along with fairly constant price hikes, the quality of the shavers has declined drastically. My first two Braun&#x27;s were high-line models and were priced around the $70 and $100 ranges, respectively. They were both clad in mostly stainless steel with only some plastic. My Activator model was mostly plastic with some stainless. The new Pulsonic has ZERO stainless: it is ALL plastic. For a nearly $300(!) MSRP shaver, this is inexcusable. In addition, the new clean &amp; renew charger base may have been simplified over the years in comparison with that of the Activator series bases, with the removal of the tower/latch design that was so problematic, but the aesthetics are lousy. The old \\&quot;metalflake\\&quot; black/dark grey thick plastic of the old base has been replaced by the cheapest el crappo dingy grey paper-thin plastic...it always looks dusty-dirty! It really looks and feels cheap and the color of it matches nothing on the shaver (or nothing else in my bathroom for that matter, LOL!). The shaver case quality has nosedived as well. My first two Brauns had padded hard zipppered nicely-lined cases covered in leatherette (\\&quot;pleather\\&quot;) with a built in shaving mirror, cleaning supplies and clear hard plastic foil cover. The Activator, at nearly double the MSRP got by with a pleather soft pouch, cheapo cleaning brush and foil cover. The new Pulsonic clear hard-plastic clamshell cover (with no room for anything else excepting a cheap cleaning brush) that looks like something the repair dept. puts on a shaver that came in with no case or on a refurbished unit. INEXCUSABLE for $300! Have you ck&#x27;ed the price for the new foil/cutter head replacement? It&#x27;s nearly DOUBLE that of the prior TOL series&#x27;s! Since they need replacement often (depending on beard toughness, shave frequency and whether or not the foil tears), add that to your operating bill along with the clean &amp; renew cartridge refills.       It&#x27;s slightly quieter than the older models duing shaving despite the new vibratory motion, but noiser during cleaning. The LCD Hygiene and Battery monitors (Model 790) are nice, as is the chrome foil/cutterblock combo plating, but the rest of the shaver is plastic and looks cheap. If you were expecting a \\&quot;statement\\&quot; shaver to set off your expensive stately Master Bath, this ain&#x27;t it (unless the statement you wanted to make is \\&quot;Hey look, I spent a fortune on an overpriced plastic POS! LOL!). Frankly, I don&#x27;t see an appreciable difference in shave closeness compared to my last Braun with both the original Activator foil/cutterblock or the \\&quot;updated\\&quot; 360 foil/cutterblock combo that I \\&quot;upgraded\\&quot; from. The shave is slightly more comfortable as the new foil design presents slightly less friction on your beard, but that&#x27;s it. Additionally, the new trimmer is awkward to use (it now sticks-out perpendicularly from the mid point of the shaver front instead of inline with the cutter head as with all previous Braun models. It is cheaply made with longevity not, apparently, a major design goal.     Finally, I don&#x27;t know when Gillette bought Braun, but it&#x27;s apparent to me that the resultant product of their parentage is to make the most expensive and best shavers on the market just the most expensive. Quality is out, while pricing is up. Do what you wish...it&#x27;s your money...but, having been there/done that/paid for it, I&#x27;d seek-out a cheaper Braun Model and save the exorbitant cost of this very gimmicky shaver. This is truly a case of \\&quot;Style Over Substance\\&quot;. I&#x27;m sure this review won&#x27;t be appreciated (my negative comments usually aren&#x27;t), but I calls &#x27;em as I sees &#x27;em! For my money, I want to know if a product is less-than what it is portrayed as in an advertisement. Hopefully, you do too.      Addendum: If you like your razor sanitary, you will be disappointed. With past self-cleaning Braun&#x27;s i.e., those with a separate foil and cutterblock, the clean and charge cartridge did a decent job of cleaning and lubing the cutting system. With the Pulsonic models, the combo one-piece foil/cutterblock allows detritus to be trapped within itself. Understand that I daily dissassemble and tap-out the excess whiskers and rinse the cutter under the sink BEFORE I use the clean and charge base auto clean. Despite this, the cutter (with it&#x27;s myriad of nooks and crannies) remains filthy...a poor design!     Update (7/22/09): FYI, the \\&quot;Clean &amp; Charge\\&quot; base station disemboweled itself this morning. While I use the auto clean function every day, I noticed my shaver was damp and didn&#x27;t smell of the cleaning fluid like it normally does. I shaved, then put the shaver in the base and pressed the \\&quot;clean\\&quot; button. After less than a minute, a big puddle appeared under the unit. I picked it up and found it was the fluid from the cleaning cartridge. I cleaned everything up and tried again...this time it emptied the cartridge (it was replaced this past week, so it was fresh)! I also noticed that the LED that signals \\&quot;empty\\&quot; doesn&#x27;t work either. Braun&#x27;s answer: \\&quot;We&#x27;re really sorry sir, take the unit and drive or ship it to the nearest service center (30-60mi away) for REPAIR\\&quot;...notice I didn&#x27;t say that they were sending me a NEW (or re-man unit, for that matter) REPLACMENT! \\&quot;You can use the power cord to charge the (dirty and getting dirtier) shaver in the meanwhile, Sir\\&quot;! WOW! Great customer service on a $300 shaver! I&#x27;ll update the sorry saga as it unfolds. On another note, the \\&quot;rebate\\&quot; that Amazon promised would be issued never came. I have to call them and get aggravated some more.     I AM TRULY SORRY THAT I EVER PURCHASED THIS THING. Buyer BEWARE!</li>

Finally I tried contacting Braun customer service for help/replacement/anything, all they would say is to send it in. I&#x27;m sorry but for a $250+ shaver I expect much more than that.  Now I&#x27;ve turned to the excellent Philips Norelco 1250 shaving system and it is great. No pulling hairs. Much better simpler cleaning system (it doesn&#x27;t use a pump) which hopefully means more reliability. I chose Philips because I have been using their sonicare toothbrushes for years and I trust the brand.     <li> so i bought one of these from amazon, very early adopter.  it is very similar in general to earlier clean and charge foil shavers from braun,  of which my last one was unceramoniously dumped in the garbage after a year for a rotary   from phillips, which was used for about another year and then dumped for the 4-blade gillette razor.  but now i&#x27;m back to trying electric for no particular reason other than it is tiresome buying   razor blade that have been specially engineered to need replacing after a week of use.  plus, while no matter what the manufacturers will tell you, there is no electric razor that  shaves as close as a blade, though sometimes the blade shaves a little too close...causing cuts, razor burn,  ingrown hairs, etc. it&#x27;s enough to make a guy want to grow a beard.    enter the braun pulsonic. this is basically a very well-made, high end \\&quot;activator\\&quot; or \\&quot;complete 360\\&quot;  with the added feature that it vibrates. i suppose this is the same technology in the gillette \\&quot;power\\&quot; series  and other regular razors that use a AAA battery to vibrate as they shave...it does result in a ever-so-slightly  better shave. so this foil, which uses the nice almost-random pattern of differently-sized holes for diffent hairs (which was avail. only in germany for a long time, for some reason, then appeared in the u.s. with the braun 360) has a nice pivoting head, standard little pop-out trimmer, and vibrates like a sonicare toothbrush while you shave. the vibration is not really noticable over the regular noise and vibration present in a regular electric razor, but the results seem to speak for themselves. it seems to be a much gentler, more effective electric razor than i have used in a long time. the only thing is, it isn&#x27;t a blade. after spending several passes with it over my cheek, for example, i can still run my hand against the growth and feel a little stubble there, which is never the case with the razor blade. on the other hand, i expect that over time there will be less shaving irritation, so it&#x27;s not a bad trade off. the thing to note is that it&#x27;s really made to be used with the little \\&quot;charge and clean\\&quot; cartridges, which according to braun last for 30 shaves, so each one lasts a month.  at $4 per cartridge, it&#x27;s not too great an expense. word of warning though: if you take the razor out of the charger before it&#x27;s finished the cleaning cycle (easy to do since much of it is silent, if you don&#x27;t wait for the &#x27;clean&#x27; light to come on) and sometimes even if you wait for it to be clean, and just start shaving, you may experience the unique and painful feeling of shaving with a small amount of rubbing alcohol on the razor foil.   i recommend making sure it&#x27;s quite dry before use, shake it a little or blow on th foil or something.  the clean and charge flud is a lemon-scented alcohol and lubricant solution that you don&#x27;t want touching newly-shaven skin.      overall, it seems to be a good investment. the razor is well-made for sure, very solid, with a rubber grip handle on the back that is pretty comfortable to hold. it moves very easily over the face, even with 3-day stubble, and is noticably more comfortable than other electrics i&#x27;ve used. i think it will take about 2 weeks for the skin/hair to get used to it again, but...good-bye razor blades! hello pulsonic!</li>

    <li> I will add my praise to the chorus of (mostly) ecstatic users.  This shaver is worth every one of the many pennies it costs.      I am a long-term user of Noreleco Rotary electric razors, always buying the top of that line.  Unfortunately, my new Norelco purchases have been coming every two years or so because something about the head mechanism always seems to break in a way which a new comb and cutter set would not fix.  Some plastic part always breaks or cracks, usually allowing the cutter assemblies to fly out of the head.  Once that happens, repair gets more expensive and time consuming and I usually just got a new one.    Even more unfortunately with each new Norelco model the battery seems weaker and the head speed slower, meaning that for best shaves the shaver must be operated in plugged in mode.  The last straw, however, was the relatively poor reviews the new Arcitec razor has been getting from users.  I decided the time had come for something different.    I did hesitate, however, having previously owned a Braun and having been underwhelmed with its heavy feel, high noise level, and huge amount of vibration.  However, given the hundreds of very positive reviews here for this latest-and-greatest model, I decided to take the plunge.    From the very first shave, I knew I would not be going back to the Norelcos.  Yes, the Braun still vibrates my hand and face more than the Norelco and is somewhat noisier.  However, the vibration now feels more like a massage and the noise was not so loud that I didn&#x27;t accommodate to it within a couple of shaves.    But the speed of the shave, the closeness of the shave, and the lack of skin irritation during and after the shave was what immediately won me over.  These are all quite superior to anything any top-of-the-line Norelco ever gave me, and they were the best electric shavers I&#x27;d ever used before.  With this Braun, I can rub may face any way I like after a shave and not feel any residual stubble.  That just wasn&#x27;t possible with any other electric shaver I&#x27;ve ever owned before.  There is no facial redness following the shave, and I can wash my face with soap immediately after the shave without any irritation from the soap.    Now we&#x27;ll see how long it lasts.  I&#x27;ve only had it for a couple of months.  It looks sturdy, with far fewer thin plastic parts than a Norelco, so I have high hopes.    The cleaning vat works as advertised, but I seem to get just as good if not better results in terms of speed, comfort, and closeness by taking the razor head off after each shave and rinsing the top of the razor and the head in a vigorous stream of very warm tap water, patting dry, air drying for awhile and then reassembling.  That process surely is quicker than using the machine.  I do smear a drop of the Braun oil across the heads once a week as recommended in the instructions if you are not constantly using the cleaning vat, which has both alcohol and an oil in the cleaning solution.</li>

    <li> Pros: Probably the best electric razor you can buy. Foil/cutterblock mechanism truly conforms to your face. Finally using lithium ion batteries.  Cons: Charge and \\&quot;hygeine\\&quot; indicators are gimmicky. Not sure what the plus/minus buttons do. No hard case. Beard trimmer has regressed from older versions. Expensive.  The magic behind the 790 is the independently-moving shaver heads. Slide your finger across the top and you&#x27;ll see that the movement mimics the independent suspension of a car. The foil/cutterblock follows the same general design Braun has been using for years now -- a trimmer for longer hairs sandwiched between two bar-shaped shaver heads -- but the independent rocking motion is new (at least to me). The shaver heads are spring-loaded and have just the right amount of give to them. Between that and the improved foil hole pattern, it now takes less strokes over my troublesome neck area to get all the weird hairs growing in different directions.  Also new is some kind of vibrational intensity adjustment, controlled by plus and minus buttons on either side of the power button. The general idea is that if the whole thing vibrates harder, it can jar those hard-to-shave hairs around and get them into the holes in the foil. This makes sense in theory but all it seems to do is make more noise. At the lowest intensity, the 790 sounds like most other Braun razors but turns into an annoying rattle at the higher setting. I&#x27;ve been using it for about ten days now, some days doing my whole shave on low, some days on high, sometimes alternating. Other than the sound, it doesn&#x27;t seem to make one bit of difference.  As you could probably guess, the two indicators on the bottom of the handle are over-designed, weird looking, and largely useless. I don&#x27;t need a battery indicator with more granularity than my cell phone; all I need to know is if it&#x27;s close to dying. And the hygiene indicator? Total gimmick. If you sprang for the deluxe model with the cleaning base, you&#x27;re probably going to follow their suggestion and drop it in every time you&#x27;re done shaving. I&#x27;ve been using Braun&#x27;s since long before the Clean &amp; Renew system and I never once thought, \\&quot;Gee, I wonder how much crap is stuck inside my shaver.\\&quot; Still, I suppose it&#x27;s not hurting anything being there.  My biggest complaint with the 790 is that for some reason they decided to swap out their usual slide-up beard trimmer for one that flips out perpendicular to the handle. It&#x27;s clumsy, difficult to open, and just doesn&#x27;t work as well. My old shaving routine involved a lot of back-and-forth between the shaving head and the beard trimmer as I would constantly switch to trimmer mode to cut long hairs that couldn&#x27;t be coaxed into the foil holes. It&#x27;s such a pain in the ass to flip up the trimmer now that I avoid it and end up more aggressively rubbing the shaver head into my neck to get these unruly stragglers.  Another dumb little thing is that they stopped making hard cases for their razors years ago. The new cases are semi-rigid plastic covered with a neoprene-like fabric. I usually bury it in my suitcase between clothes because I&#x27;m afraid that it&#x27;ll get smashed. The old hard cases could withstand getting run over by a truck. They also don&#x27;t make the little plastic shield to go over the top like they used to.  The 790 is another incremental update in the 7-Series. If you&#x27;ve never used a Braun before, you&#x27;ll definitely be in for a treat. If you&#x27;re switching from a Norelco or a Remington, you&#x27;ll never go back.</li>
    <li> In the case of this shaver, the hype really does match reality. The shaver is by far the best electric I&#x27;ve ever used, and it&#x27;s very nicely engineered--from the ergonomics of the shaving unit to the self-cleaning/lubricating mechanism that comes with the shaver. It&#x27;s a bit pricey, but you get your money&#x27;s worth out of this one.  ----------------------    After nearly two years of using this shaver I can update my original review (above) as follow:    (1) Have replaced the head once, which is right on schedule  (2) I stil love the shaves I get from this shaver.  (3) The trimmer works, but will no longer stay closed (cheap mechanism here).  (4) I&#x27;m surprised by the number of people who try to save cleaning fluid by only cleaning the head once in a while. The fact is that you can get as many cleanings as you want until evaporation requires a new cartridge. By not cleaning, you&#x27;re not saving anything.     Still give it 5-stars.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been using Norelco models, which include the 6885XL, for over 20 years. By and large, they were all very disappointing. By comparison, the Braun Pulsonic 9595CC with LCD is orders of magnitude better.     Shaving with 6885XL, I&#x27;d often end up with fair-sized sections of wholly uncut hair and of the hair it did cut, it wasn&#x27;t terribly close. It almost looked as if I didn&#x27;t shave! The Braun just wipes my face with the Norelco, so to speak. It doesn&#x27;t leave spots, period. And it&#x27;s close across my entire face. So close, I just feel skin on my cheeks. Yes, for the first time, I think I can say that electric shaving \\&quot;is there\\&quot;. It&#x27;s reached the point of doing the job it&#x27;s set out to do.  I think one of the reasons why Norelco models fail so miserably is that while their lift and cut system was patented, what actually happens is that the metal foil over the razor mats some of the hair down and the blades never get to see it. The Braun takes a different approach. The centerpiece vibrates like a little jack hammer and I&#x27;m surmising this causes the hairs to jump up tall, and the trailing half of the razor reaches them before they can bend back down. This means it does most of the work as opposed to the leading half (until you move in the other direction and their roles reverse). I don&#x27;t know if this is true, but it&#x27;s my guess behind the engineering logic. But I do know that it works!    The Braun also has another nice feature. The Norelcos store cut hair behind the foil assembly and it has to be emptied periodically. I do this over the toilet bowl and one time, the entire assembly fell into the toilet. You won&#x27;t have to worry about the Braun doing that. It comes with its own razor-washing gizmo. I haven&#x27;t had it long enough to know how it will work out long-term, but so far as I can tell, it completely cleans the razor out and it does this after every use, so long as you remember to put it back and press the clean button.     The only downside is that it&#x27;s expensive andsomewhat noisy. But it is so good otherwise, that this is almost nitpicking.     Basically, I&#x27;d say if ever other electric razor were to be discontinued tomorrow, I wouldn&#x27;t care. The Braun 9595CC stands alone as the best electric razor in the industry.</li>

But, for what they cost, I don&#x27;t think that these seven series are built like the 8995 or the one before that. I still have / own both of the predecessors to the 9595 and both still work perfectly. They are built like tanks.     Ergonimics: One thing that I didn&#x27;t like was the ergonomic design of the 7 series vs. the 8995. I found the older model easier to hold and that it had a beefier/ better build quality to it. It feels more solid to me and I can hold it from any direction and it feels great. The 9595 is contoured a bit and makes holding it from the end or upside down feel awkward.    Cleaning: THe older model is a bit quieter when cleaning and I liked the grey stand with Blue LEDs vs. the white stand. The white shows dirt and grime more and, the white one doesn&#x27;t always indicate when it&#x27;s clean as the LEDs go out after it&#x27;s been sitting for a period of time whereas the 8995 cleaning system maintains a constant \\&quot;always on\\&quot; status so you know whether it&#x27;s clean or not. I have had issues with the 9595 where it did not clean and I had no way of knowing it due to all the LEDs were out on the base. Even though I pressed the \\&quot;start cleaning\\&quot; button, and it lit up, it did not clean the shaver. This is due to how Braun designed it to be less power consuming. Whether they changed this part of the design since I got mine last season- I don&#x27;t know. It should be noted that the reason it would not clean or charge was due to the two metal electrical contacts on the base were not making good contact with the shaver. I had to use IPA to clean the contacts from oxidation and press them in and let them pop out of the shaver base as well as checking the contacts on the shaver. That part was fine. IT&#x27;s the base contacts that were the issue.    Shave quality: Both perform just as good in my experience with the newer one providing a quicker, faster cut due to higher cutting speeds but, it comes at the expense of more heat due to friction and higher vibration in the handle and cutter head. I used to cease shaving for minutes to allow it to cool down before continuing on. I used to use a light machine oil on my shaver to help prevent friction build up but, I went back to the 8995 as it works better for me. I can keep shaving with that and not get friction burned, it cleans up better, charge lasts longer, is more ergo friendly as you can hold it any direction and it feels better, there&#x27;s less vibration, the side trimmer is stronger built and is lined up directly with the cutter head to help pop lay down hairs up better than the 9595. The 9595 protrudes at an angle off the body and is not lined up with the cutter head.     I find with the 8995 that I can go sideways or along the length of the cutter head to get in extremely close. I can&#x27;t do that on the newer style 9595 cutterhead. However, for long beards or, when I haven&#x27;t shaved in a month, the 9595 does not pull. The 8995 does grab in that case. But, for everyday use, I find that both provide a very close shave.      Summary:   The 9595 and the 8995 perform equally as shavers good based on my every day use with both for about a year. The cleaning base on the 9595 is notas good as the older base and the build quality doesn&#x27;t seem as good as the 8995 based on my experience with the trimmer breaking. I also found the 9595 to become hot due to friction of the foil. Even when new, I found this to be irritating to my face. The older one runs slower cutting speeds and is cooler / less irritating.</li>
    <li> I got this to replace my 5 year old 7680 whose battery was starting to run dry. This new one&#x27;s okay, but the old model cost $50 less, cuts closer, has a better trimmer and has a more solid \\&quot;built-in-Germany\\&quot; feel to it.  The new one does not look or feel like a $200 shaver.  I&#x27;d recommend saving $50 and getting the superior 7680...</li>
    <li> This is easily the best electric shaver that I have ever used and the first that I have used outside of the Philips Norelco product line. I started with electric shavers years ago when I purchased a Norelco foil shaver. I quickly switched to a Norelco rotary shaver and used that for some time.     I&#x27;ve been using this shaver for about a week and am thoroughly impressed. The pop-up trimmer has \\&quot;Made in Germany\\&quot; written on it and you can definitely tell German engineering went into it. The shaver feels very solid and well built. Don&#x27;t get confused with the customer shot above in that the Series 7 - 790cc (9595) has an LCD display on the base to display \\&quot;battery\\&quot; and \\&quot;hygiene\\&quot; status - not a series of LEDs.    The operating controls are very simple. There is an on/off button that glows blue when the shaver is on, a tiny recessed reset button that can be pressed with a paperclip that resets the blade change counter, a button labeled \\&quot;release\\&quot; that allows the blade cartridge to be removed, and a button labeled \\&quot;lock\\&quot; that locks the shaving portion of the razor at an angle for shaving the neck. On the back of the shaver are two metal contacts for charging the unit through the supplied base and a receptacle for plugging in cord in case the battery is dead and you can&#x27;t wait for it to recharge through the base. The battery in the shaver is lithium ion (Li-ion) instead of nickel cadmium (NiCd) making battery \\&quot;memory\\&quot; problems obsolete and is advertised to run for 50 minutes before being fully discharged.     One of the biggest selling points for me on this razor was the inclusion of the self-cleaning base station. This thing is nice! When you finish shaving you simply insert the shaver into the base and the base analyzes the \\&quot;hygiene\\&quot; condition of the shaver and selects a cleaning program ranging from \\&quot;eco\\&quot; to \\&quot;intensive\\&quot; and dries the razor. The advertised cleaning time is 32 to 43 minutes depending upon the cleaning program selected and I found this to be accurate. The cleaning cartridges must be purchased separately (although one is included) and replaced every 30 days with daily use. If you&#x27;re not shaving every day it is recommended that the cleaning cartridges be replaced every eight weeks as the alcohol based cleaning solution in them evaporates over time. The base station has indicator lights on it to advise when to change the cleaning cartridges. A two pack of cleaning cartridges cost me approximately $8.00 at a local store.    The only other ongoing cost associated with this shaver is the replacement of the cutter cassette that is recommended every 18 months and run approximately $30.00. Compared to the high cost of disposable razors that must be purchased constantly and the convenience of not having to clean this razor it is a steal! The only problem I have run into with this unit is that it does leave some stubble on the neck area especially around the Adam&#x27;s Apple but as I have continued to learn how to best use this shaver it has gotten much better. I have serious problems shaving irritating my skin after shaving and I have thus has to wait several days between shaves. With this shaver I can now shave every other day with absolutely no problems. It also gives me the closest shave that I have ever had with an electric shaver and it rivals regular disposable razors. Overall, I highly recommend this shaver to anyone new to electric shavers or looking for a replacement.</li>

    <li> Just got this shaver as a Christmas gift from my wife, and I must say it is awesome! The shave I am getting after initial use is on par with what I get with a Fusion razor. I have sensitive skin and get painful razor burn after every shave with regular razors - Mach 3, Sensor, Fusion - did not matter, shaving was a painful experience. Which is why I never shaved everyday. Just hated it. Not to mention putting on cold shaving gel early in the morning during the winters. With the razor and because of razor burn, I could not shave closely along my jawline and on my neck for fear of getting sensitivity, rashes, redness and cuts in that area. No such problem with the Pulsonic. As such, I can potentially get a better shave with an electric shaver than a razor. I am still trying the Pulsonic out, and they say it takes a good three weeks for your face to get adjusted to a new shaver. Good thing Braun provides a 30-day guarantee - though I do not anticipate taking them up on that offer. Even with a couple of shaves, I am getting as close a shave as my razor. And the razor burn is gone!    My previous experience with an electric shaver was 8 years ago, when I purchased a then-topline Norelco rotary model (6000-series, if I remember correctly).  I wanted to switch to electrics back then for the same reason I want to switch now: painful razor burn and messy shaving creams/gels. Unfortunately, the Norelco rotary system gave me lots of in-grown hairs, especially on my neck and near the jaw line. Also, the shaver never properly captured all the shaved hairs, leaving a mess on the sink for me to clean, as well having to clean the shaver itself - double work and an annoyance. Each person&#x27;s face and hair is different and they react differently to rotary versus foil electric shavers. I gave up on the Norelco because of the hassles and grudgingly went back to old fashioned razors. I guess I should have tried the Braun shavers first instead.    I had been keeping an eye out for the newBraun models, especially when they came out with the cleaning systems few years ago. Minimalist industrial design and generally built like tanks at a slightly premium price - that was my general impression of the Braun shavers. But having spent money on the Norelco and being burned, I did not risk making another purchase then and wasting more money. Well, I am glad I waited till they introduced the Pulsonic model and my wife got me the 9595.    The Pulsonic 9595 deals with nearly all the complaints I had with electric shavers, and based on my brief usage, I believe it will give me a great shave as well. The cleaning system is pure genius in my opinion: makes daily use of the shaver as simple as taking it off the cleaning station, turning on the shaver and shaving, followed by simply placing the shaver back in its resting spot and pressing the \\&quot;start cleaning\\&quot; button. The station literally takes care of everything else - from analyzing the level of cleaning needed, to cleaning and lubricating the shaver head and blades, to drying out the shaver head for the next shave and keeping the shaver fully charged. This is really a fool-proof system they have developed. Curiously, the shaver comes out smelling like lemon pledge because the alcohol bath has a lemon scent.    Only down side is that the cleaning solution needs to be replaced about once per month, but the cost is reasonable (especially with the Amazon subscription) compared to the wonderful job the cleaning system does keeping the shaver cleaned and ready every time. Nice of Braun to continue using the same cartridge design across all their models - in sharp contrast to their cousins in the Gillette division. Compared to previous Braun shavers, the Pulsonic has a lithium battery, so keeping the shaver in the cleaning base plugged in all the time is not an issue. Plus the base is smart enough to turn itself off after 10 minutes of inactivity so that it does not continuously juice the lithium battery (overnight, forexample). Like I said, Braun has developed an incredibly smart system of shaver maintenance. I am very impressed. The only complaint I have is the quality of the plastic used in the outer shell of the cleaning station - feels very cheap and fragile. Especially for the price one pays for the whole package, they should have used better materials.    The shaver itself thankfully suffers from no such faults. While it is plastic, the quality of the materials used in the body is top notch, and the shaver exudes a sturdy feel to it. And despite what the product images on the packaging and on web sites may indicate, most of the body is covered in a quality rubber like material that helps maintain a good grip while shaving. The LCD display at the bottom is nice, showing battery level and how dirty the shaver is since the last cleaning. Given the ~$40 MSRP difference between the 9595 and 9585, the extra cost is not worth it since the only difference between the two models is level of information shown for battery and cleaning needs on the shaver. However, most online stores are selling both models at almost the same prices - so might as well purchase the topline model.     The shaver has lithium ion batteries - generally believed to have better performance compared to the Ni-Cad batteries all other previous Braun shavers had. Another very nice feature is the ability to use the shaver while plugged in with the auto-detect wall charging plug, and not having to wait for the shaver to recharge before you start using it. The shaver also has a 5-minute quick charge feature.     There have been some complaints about the travel case. While I do not have the previous Braun model&#x27;s travel cases for comparison, I like the hard plastic tube that the Pulsonic can be stored in. It protects the whole shaver when it might get banged around in the luggage during travel. There is even a small space to store a cleaning brush in the case - makes sense since you will need it to clean the shaverwhen away from home and not have access to the cleaning base. People have also mentioned that there is no plastic clip to protect the shaving head, unlike other shavers that include such a thing. I don&#x27;t think it is necessary: I store the shaver in the cleaning base when at home, and in the travel case when traveling, and don&#x27;t feel the need to have a plastic clip for the head.    I can see now why the reviews on this model have been almost universally stellar - and why this shaver is sold out almost every where. Sure there are some detractors - understandable since not every man&#x27;s face and beard is the same. There is that 30-day guarantee, just in case. But I do not hesitate in recommending this shaver. Braun really as produced a great shaver - both in terms of shaving and ease of use.</li>

    <li> I got the Pulsonic 9595 for Christmas this year. After a few weeks, I have learned that to catch the neck hairs and some of the odd jawbone area hairs, you have to be creative with which direction you pass the head over your face. I kind of go sideways first, then I Invert the razor (power button down) and drag it upwards to finish it off. The razor has a meter which keeps track of the \\&quot;hygiene\\&quot; of the razor head. I think it is actually a glorified usage timer, but at any rate, the more tick marks that are missing, the more intense the cleaning it recommends. I have cleaned mine every day on eco mode and the fluid is still on the \\&quot;high\\&quot; mark meaning I still have a lot of fluid left after 25 days of use. I also like the fact that it comes with a hard carrying case that you can put the shaver into when travelling. When travelling, you just take the plug from the base and plug it into the razor for charging. If you are only going for a day or 2, the plug would not even be needed, as the battery life would be plenty for a short trip. When travelling, you can just take the head off the unit and rinse the razor to clean. I would definately recommend this razor for someone wanting to get an electric.</li>

    <li> I typically don&#x27;t write reviews, even on products that give extraordinary results.  So, you know this is an atypical review from the outset. I&#x27;ve also tried several Norelco shavers with the floating heads and lift-and-cut cutters, but they took too much work and way too long to give an adequate shave.    After reading well over 100 reviews about many different makes and models of shavers, I decided to give the Braun Pulsonic System 9595 a try.  I was a little skeptical after reading some of the reviews, but I made up my mind to give it several weeks for my skin to adjust to the newly designed shave head, even though I had been using a Braun up until that time. It is much quieter than my previous Braun, and it&#x27;s as though I&#x27;m getting a face and neck massage as I&#x27;m shaving each morning.  As I&#x27;ve learned over the past month or so, the key to getting a consistent, close shave is holding the shaver at a 90 degree angle to the area you&#x27;re shaving.  It also helps to pull the skin tight and shave against the growth grain.    I&#x27;ve read some complaints about the trimmer but have found it to be both precise and effective.  I also like the fact that it protrudes at a 90 degree angle so you can be very precise with it in tight areas.    Overall, I am well pleased with this shaver and highly recommend it.  Not only does it give a close, smooth, irritation-free shave, it&#x27;s a pleasure to use.    Oh, I almost forgot about the lock on the shaver head.  I&#x27;ve read where some have had problems getting it to lock.  However, the key to it is to allow the head to tilt back as the lock is being pushed into the locked position.  Once it&#x27;s locked, the head is actually tilted forward, so it&#x27;s much easier to maintain a 90 degree angle in some of the hard to reach spots.  Then, to remove the lock, simply push it in the opposite direction to allow the shaver head to glide freely.    Finally, while the shaver is not inexpensive, I feel it&#x27;s well worth the investment.  I also like the cleaning system, which I use daily to keep the shaver head clean and lubricated.  I can definitely tell a difference in the closeness of the shave and how more easily it glides along the face and neck areas.    Happy shaving!    Jim</li>

But, there is NO discomfort with the Braun Pulsonic as there is with a blade. Some people say the cleaning system is not as good as the razor, being expensive, noisy, etc. I agree that it is rather noisy, but if you think about the ease of use factor, it&#x27;s not that expensive. The cleaning system cleans, lubricates, and dries the shaver, and very well at that. You don&#x27;t have to worry about leaving it open to dry after rinsing it clean, or lubricating it once a week, since the water doesn&#x27;t lubricate it. The solution has a semi-pleasant, citrus smell. The unit remembers how much it&#x27;s been run since the last cleaning, and the base adjusts the cleaning cycle to that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;easy to use&lt;br /&gt;comfortable on your face&lt;br /&gt;ergonomical (for me anyway)&lt;br /&gt;close (let your face get used to it for a while before you judge)&lt;br /&gt;built very solid&lt;br /&gt;cartridges of solution make for easy changing (no bottles to mess with)&lt;br /&gt;base is reasonably sized, especially compared to a cleaning base for a rotary shaver, which doesn&#x27;t heat dry it&lt;br /&gt;has a lcd to remind you when to change the foil and cutter&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning cycles are reasonably noisy&lt;br /&gt;cleaning cartridges represent additional expense (although only about $5.50 a cartridge, which should last almost two months if you clean every other shave, {get it down so there&#x27;s two bars left in the hygiene meter, so it&#x27;ll stay on the normal clean cycle.})&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Final Thoughts:&lt;br /&gt;I paid $130 two years ago for a self cleaning rotary shaver. this is not even twice the price, and is MUCH more than twice as good. I will never go back to a rotary. Reasonably priced, although it could be a little cheaper, maybe around $180 would be the price at which I wouldn&#x27;t go with ANYTHING else.</li>

    <li> Ok, so after reading the reviews of others let me summarize. All but the occasional outlier agree that this is an excellent razor. The dispute largely comes from the majority who are completely pleased with their purchase, and a significant minority who think the razor is overpriced. I&#x27;m with the minority. As to the quality issue--no issue there. Excellent razor, smoother and a bit quicker in shave than my old Remington Titanium 5520, probably a bit closer shaver, too. Perhaps it is most accurate to focus on the \\&quot;quicker\\&quot; rather than \\&quot;closer.\\&quot; That is, it gets to where it&#x27;s going a LITTLE faster than my older, cheaper shaver. However (updating this review after months of use, when the blades are no longer quite as new...), areas that the Remington was not perfect on, the Braun doesn&#x27;t do significantly better either. That&#x27;s my face-- and that&#x27;s the state of electric razor technology. There&#x27;s been no magic bullet. This is not an amazing new technology, Braun&#x27;s marketing success with \\&quot;pulsonic\\&quot; notwithstanding. If you now feel compelled to touch up on important days with a blade--you still will after buying this. Another performance related issue deserves comment--the oft-mentioned noise issue. I don&#x27;t get that complaint. This is quieter than the Remington, nothing more than a significant hum. On the whole I&#x27;m very pleased with it. But all that said--is it worth the price? That&#x27;s the real issue. I got this at the discounted price, including cleaning base system, of $219 and free shipping. The Remington, which used to be pricier, is available now for about $50 these days. Is the Braun 400%+ better? Not hardly. Over four times the price (even with new discounts) and not even 50% better is more like it. And 50% would be high. Play with the math, but you get the idea: the difference is evolutionary, not revolutionary, and those who wax poetic about getting what you pay for are perhaps overly defensive over their spending habits. :) This is an improvement over the lower endrazors--but neither indispensable nor magical. (A lot of the price hike goes to bells and whistles, of course. Having a \\&quot;hygiene meter\\&quot; hardly gives you a closer shave, for instance.) My ultimate decision: keep it. It&#x27;s classy and excellent. It is used every day. And will last years. Under those circumstances, spending extra for some modest improvement is worth it to me as the cost is amortized by both frequency of use and the time it is likely to last.  A lot of that decision to keep it is centered around inertia, however. It is a hassle to send it back and start looking again, and I might be no happier in Round 2. It is not worth the effort for the $75 or whatever that I perhaps overpaid. I probably won&#x27;t buy a similarly priced model next time around. You&#x27;ll be pleased. You&#x27;ll see some improvement (smoothness, in particular). But as with most luxury products, when you troll for \\&quot;best ofs,\\&quot; the hideous price spike rarely makes you think you are getting value for the extra money, even if it is better.</li>

The answer is that it depends on the blade.  It doesn&#x27;t shave as close as my fusion power with my good shave cream and brush in the shower.  But it does shave as close as ANY 2 bladed razor out there and possibly as close as the Mach 3.  Basically if you shave very close with a razor and wait about 1/2 hour and feel your face, that is how close this shaver shaves (and that is pretty darn close).  And my face hasn&#x27;t even adjusted yet.  I&#x27;ll try to update this review after 3 weeks, but I am totally happy with it right now, it can only get better as my face adjusts.    This shaver is DEFINITELY worth every penny.  Don&#x27;t skimp on a lower model to save a few bucks, you&#x27;ll be happy you didn&#x27;t.  That said, I don&#x27;t know how the top of the line models from Norelco or Panasonic are... They are probably very good too, but I cannot imagine that they could be any better.    UPDATE 2/23/10:    I&#x27;ve been using this shaver for 1.5 months now and I have to say I love it more than I did when I first wrote this review.    The shaver produces a close comfortable shave right out of the box the first time you use it, but after about a month, is is even better.  From what I understand that is because your face adjusts.  Whatever the reason, I am getting the absolute best shaves of my life, with little or no irritation!!    I have thrown out all of my old razors and shave cream.  I will NEVER go back to a blade!    I am amazed to actually be saying this, but this shaver is that good.    I also recommend using \\&quot;Lectric Shave\\&quot; pre-shave.    I used to loathe shaving and avoid it at all costs, now I look forward to shaving.    I cannot recommend this shaver enough.</li>

    <li> This razor is an excellent quality product. I suspect it will last a loooong time. The blades need changing at about the 18 month time. It has a good internal 3.8V LiOn battery and does a decent job shaving. The only issue I&#x27;ve had in two years use is the board containing the battery can move slightly if the shaver is accidentally dropped or jarred (maybe in the clean up cycle?}. The springy contacts from the battery control board to the motor housing don&#x27;t make contact causing the shaver to stop. It is an easy fix by prying on the sides of the rubber housing with a thin blade screwdriver to remove it exposing the second cover. Undoing the 4 screws and removing the second cover exposes the battery compartment and control board. The copper contact pins from the battery board need to be stretched out slightly so they contact the motor housing firmly. Reassemble and you are ready to go. All in all this is a well made shaver and does a good job for me.</li>

    <li> I bought this shaver in 2009 and imagine I can give a pretty thorough review at this point.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First of all, let&#x27;s address the question of electric shavers.  Will it shave as close as a blade?  Absolutely not.  And it is not designed to do that.  Will you LOOK like it shaved as close as a blade?  Yes you will, if you take the time to let your face get used to it and stop using a blade you will look like you spend a lot more time shaving than you actually do.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ll start with the Pros to buying/using this shaver.  The design is great and it does not feel &#x27;cheap&#x27;.  it offers a good shave early in the morning when I am less than awake and it cleans itself so I don&#x27;t have to remember to take it apart and clean it.  The battery lasts forever (even after two years) so if you go on a business trip, you don&#x27;t have to take the cleaning base with you.  Also, if you need to be away for a really long time, like more than a week, the same cord that plugs into the cleaning base plugs into the shaver itself so you can recharge it on the go.  The cleaning fluid is nice for people who are prone to bad complexion because it sterilizes the razor after every use and an electric shaver is less harsh on your skin after your face gets used to it.  Also, I cannot prove that the pulsonic aspect of this shaver is \\&quot;better\\&quot; than other shavers but I definitely shave faster with this one than any other one I have owned before.  It is also much faster than using a traditional razor and shaving creme.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now for the Cons, such that they are.  First and foremost, you have to remember to shave before you get in the shower and get your skin wet.  It took me a while to change my routine.  If you have not used an electric shaver before, you need to let your face have time to get used to it.  Most people/companies say give it 30 days.  I say give it a bit longer but that is only my personal opinion.  I have a pretty rough beard and it took longer for my face to adapt to the waythis thing cuts.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One design flaw, after about a year, the silver coloring near the pivot of the razor started to peel off a bit.  Braun offered to replace it but I just never remembered/had the time to ship it back.  I applaud their customer service but wish it had not happened to begin with.  Still, it is only a cosmetic issue and does not affect the operation of the shaver (and in all honesty, I am NOT gentle with anything at 7am).  This would not keep me from buying another of their products but feel it should be mentioned.  I subtracted a star for this but it should really only be about a half star.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for cost:  I have tried to estimate the cost of shaving with a traditional razor (mach 3 etc) and shaving cream vs using the Braun Plusonic and the cleaning fluid.  Keep in mind that Braun recommends that you buy a new cutting head every 16 months which costs about $50.  The cleaning refills cost about $16 for three (average, sometimes you can find them on sale for better) and last right at 30 days each.  All in all, including cost of upfront purchase, it seems that the Braun may be a few dollars more but they are pretty close so cost really should not be a huge factor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My shaver is still working fine.  I have used it every day for two years and see no reason why I wont for two more years.  Overall, I am happy with the purchase.  It does exactly what it says; shaves the fuzzy stuff off your face and cleans itself.  If you are on the fence about electric shavers, give this one a try.  They are not for everyone but I have not bought a traditional razor in two years.  Take that for what it is worth.</li>

    <li> Bought this shaver for my husband. He loves it!!! Here&#x27;s my husband&#x27;s review: If you haven&#x27;t figured it out yet, the new Braun Pulsonic is even better as a wet shaver. Notice that it says WASHABLE in letters you can&#x27;t miss on the front of the shaver. Simply wet your face, put on some Gillette Foamy shaving cream, and get ready for an incredibly close shave!! If you want an even closer shave, FIRST shave ONLY WITH THE GRAIN of your beard (NOT against the grain)using a typical Gillette double or triple blade. Then finish up with the Pulsonic. This seems to get the longer, flat lying hairs a little better. After all, it&#x27;s the shaving AGAINST the grain of your beard with a blade that produces the nicks and iritation.     <li> First, a little background: I&#x27;ve been a loyal razor shaver for the last 4-5 years. My first electric shaver was a cheap Remington that didn&#x27;t work back in 2002. That made me anti-electric razor for years. However, as the years have gone by I&#x27;ve realized I&#x27;m one of the lucky ones to have sensitive skin and ingrown neck hairs due to razor shaving. I did my research and everyone recommends electric shavers.    After a lot of research I bought the Braun 9595. A lot of my friends were long time Braun users and highly recommended the brand as well. My friend even gave me a free 3 cleaning pack as a welcome into the Braun club. :)    The Braun 9595 is a great shaver. It is a lot quieter than other electric shavers I&#x27;ve seen and it does cut a whole lot better as well. I really like the pivoting head as it makes for a really comfortable shave. However, I learned the hard way that you have to shave against the grain with Electric shavers (unlike razor blades).    Although this shaver doesn&#x27;t shave as close as my old 5 blade Razor - I&#x27;ve already seen noticeable decrease in razor burn (even on day 2). I definitely recommend this for you guys like me who have a problem with razor burn on their neck. The pop out trimmer is perfect for stubborn hair that doesn&#x27;t want to pop out (ingrown hair). Just make sure to shave against the grain really slowly and not with it.    The cleaning system is really amazing. After you get done shaving just stick the shaver into the base and it automatically detects the cleaning level. After you hit the center button the shaver turns on and you can hear the cleaning solution going through it. Just be aware that it takes a good set of minutes before the cleaning is done. The refills are supposed to last 30 days so I clean the shaver every 2 shaves (1 cleaning refill should last 2 months). After 2 shaves the shaver says it wants a Normal Clean (as I clean it with water anyway). After the automatic cleaning is done the shaver head has a nice lemon smellto it (not overpowering in the least bit).    A big concern of mine was the ability to travel with this shaver. This shaver has a place to plug in the electrical cord directly (though you can normally recharge it through the base). I travel now and then so this was a big deal for me. I recommend this for people who do a lot of traveling.    The cleaning solution is made in Ireland and the Braun Pulsonic 9595 itself is made in Germany. A FYI if you are interested in that sort of stuff like I am.    Something to note: As a guy coming from razor blades into the electric shaver world - my face gets really dry after a shave now. You might want to have some lotion handy to relieve the dryness.      Without a doubt I would highly recommend this shaver to anyone - especially for guys like me who get razor burn using razor blades. It sure is a nice feeling knowing I won&#x27;t be buying $24 razor blade replacements every 2 months...</li>

    <li> After years of using a Norelco rotary shaver, I decided to \\&quot;upgrade\\&quot; to the new Pulsonic line.  I received the 790cc as a Christmas present and have been mostly satisfied with its performance after using it for several weeks.    All the Braun marketing hype surrounding their 7 series shavers is accurate, to a point.  The 790cc beats my older Norelco hands-down.  The shave is closer, quicker and gives my skin way less irritation.  I hardly need to apply after shave to soothe my skin.  While my old rotary was by no means a bad shaver, it often left my entire neck red.  I hardly have that problem with the Norelco.  This is the closest shave I&#x27;ve received with an electric shaver.      The Pulsonic technology definitely helps stand your whiskers on edge.  Provided you follow the customary electric shaver practice of stretching your skin, running the blades against the grain and holding the shaver at a 90-degree angle, you&#x27;ll be more than happy with the results.  That said, it still falls short of a manual wet shave.  Even with the Pulsonic feature, the Power Comb and the locking head, I usually have to go over my neck two or three times for an ideal shave.    The charging and cleaning base station uses a mixture of alcohol, lubricant and fragrance to clean your shaver.  The status indicator on the bottom of the shaver indicates the battery life and hygiene level of the unit, letting you know when its time to cradle the shaver.  The base station automatically selects the necessary cleaning cycle.  Not only is the base station convenient, but it helps reduce skin irritation when you shave by keeping the blades clean, dry and well-lubricated.    For such an expensive shaver, I would have preferred a better carrying case.  The flimsy plastic case provided houses the shaver and a cleaning brush for the road, but no place to put the charger or bottle of appliance oil.  As another reviewer mentioned, the shaver is built extremely well, but the aesthetic choices made by Braun are a little mish-mashed.  The shaver, the base station and the charger are all different colors.  Despite what product pictures may lead you to believe, the shaver&#x27;s LCD display is not backlit, so it can be challenging to read under the direct glare of your bathroom&#x27;s lights.  All these issues are minor and hardly a deal-breaker.    If you&#x27;re looking to save some money, buy the 760cc instead of this particular model.  The only difference is the shaver&#x27;s display indicator (it&#x27;s an LED instead of an LCD) and the base station&#x27;s fast clean feature (there isn&#x27;t one).    I look forward to using my Braun as my primary shaver for years to come.</li>

Other than that performs well and much less bulky. I like it! Worth the investment after several years of my old Braun.</li>

If I forgo the cleaning and just charge the razor it makes a very high frequency buzz once its done charging that makes it rather uncomfortable to just be in the same room.     <li> This is definitely the the Rolls Royce of shavers.      Let me first say that I hated shaving.  I tried numerous electrics but always ended up with the latest \\&quot;safety razor\\&quot;.  Which ever one had the most blades and promised the most comfort.  I never found any of them comfortable and I always broke out or got razor burn.  I disliked shaving so much that I only shaved when I absolutely needed to.      Now that I have the Series 7, I find myself shaving just for the hell of it.  After about the first week or so I have very little, if any, irritation during or after shaving.  It is very convenient being able to shave before showering and its even encouraged.  Prior to using this, in order for me to shave I practically needed an aseptic surgical-like environment.  Now I rub this thing on my face for a few minutes and I&#x27;m out the door.      I think the LCD on the bottom of the razor is kind of overkill.  The information it displays is very vague (just little boxes displaying how dirty the razor is and how much battery life is left) compared to the previous models LCD.  The Series 5 razor had a scrolling text display that actually told you how minutes you had left before the battery died and other important information.  If the LCD is part of your decision making between the 790cc and the 760cc then I would say go for the 760cc.    Overall, I am satisfied with my purchase and would recommend this product to anyone who absolutely dreaded shaving as much as I did.  It takes a little bit longer for a full shave, but if you keep up with the growth its not bad at all.  I would trade an extra 3 minutes off the morning routine for decreased irritability any day.   There is certainly a high price tag but in this case I believe you get what you are paying for.</li>

    <li> To start off I am 41 years old and have been using electric shavers for 25 years. Blade shavers destroy my face and my beard is so tough and thick that they never worked for me.  I have mainly owned Norelco&#x27;s over this time.  The only experience I have had with a foil electric was with cheap Panasonics I bought when I was younger (like $19.99).  Back when I used these they worked very well but the foil would wear down or break too soon and cut me. From there I purely have been using each Norelco or other kinds of lift and cut systems.    The 9595 is my first try at a foil in a long time.  Unlike many reviews here you can look at my history and see my review for the top of the line Norelco that I&#x27;ve had for about 2 1/2 years.  I can say that I was satisfied with the Norelco and if the Pulsonic had not had a good review at Gizmodo.com I would not have even looked at it.  Once I came and started reading reviews I became very interested.  I hate HATE shaving to the point where I usually shave about every 4 days.  I work at home so I don&#x27;t need the \\&quot;office\\&quot; look.  Let me compare the two shavers for a true review of the advantages in the 9595.  First of all when I opened the box and put in the cleaning cartridge I noticed that the cleaner system is about 1000% better and easier than the Norelco system.  The Norelco system requires you to pull apart the case and pour the liquid into a tiny hole - and then screw it shut and put it back onto the base and let the liquid flow in. Also, when you add more liquid you must clean the dissolved hair from the cleaning system.  It&#x27;s messy and a pain in the ass.  However I will say that the cleaning system did make each shave in effect seem like I was using a new razor which is what the purpose was.  Another defect was that it takes forever to clean, and then you must take it out and lay it down to dry (or put it back in the system to rest but that takes longer).  The Pulsonic is designed beautifully.  You take the cartridge and put itin... that&#x27;s the complete effort.  Then when it&#x27;s empty you get a new one.  That alone may have convinced me to get a new shaver - the ease is terrific. Also unlike the Norleco where once it&#x27;s done shaving and charging you have to take it out to get it to stop (make the charge and cleaning lights go off) the Pulsonic cleans and then blow dries it with heat!  No need to ever take it out - it goes off when it&#x27;s done - fantastic.  The one noticable disadvantage of the Pulsonic cleaning system is that it&#x27;s NOISY and it takes much longer.  By noisy I mean SHUT THE DOOR noisy. The Noreclo wasn&#x27;t quiet but this is just LOUD.  So the conclusion for the cleaning system is that it&#x27;s heads and tails better than the Norelco system.  If not for the time and noise it would be 100%.  Onto the shave.  The Norelco was a fairly slow shaver to shave with.  Yes, you could get a close shave with it after about 13-15 minutes but you had to keep going over areas.  Also it was terrible on the neck - it just misses hairs until you go over and over them.  I got so bored with it that I started shaving it with it while browsing on the computer and then finished off in front of a mirror.  Did it do it&#x27;s job?  YES.  Was the shave good?  YES.  But it was slow and took real effort to do a good job.  The only part of my face that I noticed that the Norelco did a better job than the Pulsonic was my lower chin.  And that&#x27;s a review after only one use.  I may learn to get that area better in the future.  Onto the Pulsonic.  Today was my first try with 4 days of beard growth.  heavy and grey in many spots on the chin area.    Let me make one thing clear to those comparing a blade to an electric shaver.  You will ALWAYS get a faster closer shave with a blade.  The blade is ON YOUR SKIN taking the hair and skin off as you shave.  I don&#x27;t know how anyone would think you can get closer than that.  With ANY electric shaver you are going to have to go over areas more than once - it&#x27;s a given and there is noway to avoid it.  So stop saying the blade is closer etc.. of course it is.  The Pulsonic took me about half the time that the Norelco did - about 6 or 7 minutes and this was just my first try.  It does get FAR more hair off on every try and it is WAY faster.  I found that I could shave most areas extremely quickly - I was amazed at how fast it was.  I was blown away at the speed that it took the hair off compared to what I&#x27;ve been using.  Now if I had just gone over my face once with this it would have been just an OK shave.  But you can&#x27;t do that with an electric shaver as I explained.  I found that going over the areas fast a few times got me a very very close shave without missing anything.  The tough areas were the chin and neck - but it still did my neck way way faster than the Norelco.  The Pulsonic really takes the hair off - the power difference is extremely noticable - it&#x27;s like replacing an old lawn mower with a turbo.  There is one negative - and it&#x27;s the same as the negative with the cleaning - it SOUNDS like it&#x27;s powerful.  The noise is about 10 times what my Norelco was making.  It&#x27;s LOUD.  Not just a little loud - real loud - shut the door loud.  As far as the form I found it fit in my hand just fine.  I used it without the lock the first time and I will play with it as time goes on.  Also I noticed that like any other new shaver you need to learn how to shave with it - there is a method.  This should speed up the process and get my a closer shave faster.  How close is the shave compared to the Norelco or any other shaver I&#x27;ve ever used?  WAY closer.  As I said above - just going over it once is not going to do it - go over it until you can feel with your hand that the shave is close.  I asked my wife how my skin felt afterwards and she said it was incredibly close - much closer than anything I&#x27;ve ever used.  In fact I am feeling my face now and I can tell that it&#x27;s the closest shave I ever have had.  Finally the Pulsonic 9595 is a beautiful piece of design and looks more like a small coffee maker than a shaver.  It&#x27;s white with bright blue lights and looks terrific.  Way better than the Norelco system I had.  I would recommend this for anyone who uses an electric shaver who wants a top notch designed system and about the closest shave I think an electric will give you.  If you are considering moving from a blade to an electric then expect to have to put some more effort into getting close.    The plastic carrying case is fine - sure it&#x27;s ugly plastic but who really cares?  The Norelco had a fancy black case but I found it bulky and hard to close.    Ah one last bad thing about the design I just recalled.  The plug on the Pulsonic does not stretch very far. You will need to put the base near the plug because it&#x27;s one of those stretchy cords.  My old Norelco had a standard cord and could be put anywhere on my sink area.  Also the plug on this really sticks out FAR.  I don&#x27;t know the logic they used to make it not flush with the wall but it&#x27;s not even close.  Feel free to post questions.  FYI - I don&#x27;t work for Braun or Norelco. I am a founder and run Toldya.com... a website.  UPDATE!  After owning this since January of 2008 I am finding that it&#x27;s breaking down.  I just had to throw away the cleaning unit because it got clogged up and was leaking the cleaning solution all over the place.  I attempted to clean it out and put a fresh cartridge in but it leaked again.  It&#x27;s not worth it for me to call and get a replacement so I threw it in the garbage.  The shaver still works great but the head doesn&#x27;t move as well and the lock mechanism is cheap and broken.  Hopefully water will clean it well or I will need a new shaver.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been shaving with electric razors for over 20 years, and I&#x27;ve always had problems with razor-burn around my jaw and neckline despite trying several popular preshave products and razors.     <li> I am using the shaver now for 4 months. The shaver itself works very well. I like especially the cleaning station which leaves the shaver in top condition and completely clean from the inside. I am wondering however if the daily charging that comes with each cleaning is not draining the capacity of the battery more rapidly. I hope the charger is a trickle charger. The cleaning solution lasts for almost exactly one month, also as advertised.    Ok, so why am I giving this unit only 1 star? Because the power adapter failed me after 4 months and the rigid service system Braun has behind its products is not acceptable by a long shot. The $215 shaver comes with a 2 year warranty that covers parts like these. Unlike many other companies who sent you a new replacement/exchange part in a matter of 2-3 business days after asking a few questions on the phone, Braun gives you the run-around. First you need to call the central service line, where your concern is simply noted. You are then forwarded to a local/regional service center that actually needs to looks at the unit. These are little shops to which Braun has outsourced the actual repair. No big thing I thought. By connecting the power adapter directly to the shaver it became clear right away that the power adapter was broken (no blinking of segments).  In my case my closest service center was in Woodland Hills with the encouraging name \\&quot;Speedy Appliances\\&quot;. Luckily I decided to not follow the advice of the central Braun service to send the entire unit including shaver to that location. Instead I drove the 15 miles down there on a sunny morning, hoping I could leave with a new adapter. Sure enough the staff there determined in 1 minute that the unit was indeed broken and that this would we a warranty case. Without looking anywhere in his store he said that he would need to order the adapter. It turned out that that it would take about 2-3 weeks and that the adapter would first need to be shipped to his store and then he would ship it to my address adding another few days to it. There was no way that the unit could be drop shipped directly to me. When calling the central Braun line the next business day asking them if this of-the-shelf adapter could not be shipped directly, I got the same \\&quot;we are not flexible\\&quot; approach. Any warranty part needs to go out to the service center first. Alternatively I could order the unit also directly from the parts center in which case it would ship directly to me, but I also would need to pay for everything.   Afterwards I called the parts line directly to see out of curiosity what the power adapter costs and how long it takes them to ship to me: $21 plus $5 S&amp;H, in stock, could be there in 5-7 business days.  If Braun would use batteries that last 4-6 weeks I would give them all the time in the world to work in the archaic, snail-paced service world, but the battery lasts about 1.5 weeks if used daily. And daily use is the whole idea behind a shaver and many other Braun products isn&#x27;t it...  Luckily I still have my older high-end Norelco, who will serve me well while Braun gets my adapter mailed around the US. So, don&#x27;t toss your old unit yet if you decide to buy this product. You might need it sooner rather than later.</li>

    <li> I am one of those individuals who use an electric shaver out of necessity, rather than just personal preference. From time to time, I have used razor blades, disposable or high-end, only to have my face transformed into something looking like hamburger. Call me a baby face if you like, but electric shavers have been the only shaving device that have kept my morning shaving routine from resembling some sort of torture session.    Consequently, I have gone through 25+ years of adulthood going from one electric shaver to the next; always with the hope for that perfect shave, but always left wanting. Having said that, Braun shavers have always been my default electric shaver. While I have occasionally tried other brands, I always found myself coming back to Braun and their reliable foil shavers; they always seemed to outperform all the others.    While Braun shavers \\&quot;got the job done\\&quot;, they too had their shortcomings: they always seemed to 1) leave me with that occasional razor burn, 2) be unable to closely shave those one or two awkward places on my face, and 3) take too long to get the job done - sometime requiring several passes across the same place to get an even reasonably close shave. But having tried multiple electric shavers, I had convinced myself that this was as good as it was going to get. However, I continued to hold out hope that something better might eventually come along...    Enter the Braun Pulsonic 9595! After reading several of the reviews of this shaver, I was intrigued. However, to say that I suffered from sticker shock, would be an understatement. \\&quot;Surely no electric shaver could possibly be worth that kind of money, could it?\\&quot; Following several months of mental debate and calisthenics, I finally decided to take the plunge about three months ago. \\&quot;Could this finally be the one?!\\&quot;    In short, yes, it could and it is! This shaver is different than anything else I have ever used. The pulsonic technology is not just a marketing gimmick, it really works. Here&#x27;s been the impact: razor burns have been non-existent, my daily shaving time has been decreased by a third, and close shaves have become the norm, rather than the exception. Let me provide a few specifics and personal recommendations.    The owner&#x27;s manual, similar to most Brauns, recommend using the shaver before washing your face. That may work for some people, but not for me. Washing my face, then allowing at least 15 minutes for it to completely dry has provided the most comfortable and close shave. Second, pressing harder with this shaver actually makes it less effective. I know this is counter-intuitive, but it must have to do with the pulsonic technology. So, if you encounter a patch of whiskers or a certain part of your face that is particularly uncooperative, make a light pass across the area with the shaver. If your experience is like mine, you&#x27;ll be amazed that the hair instantly disappears.  Over time, I&#x27;ve gradually trained myself to shave, while applying less pressure with the shaver. This has resulted in quicker and closer shaves!    This is the first time I have owned an electric shaver with a cleaning system. The LCD screen indicates the shaver needs to be cleaned after about every three shaves, even though the charge lasts for 5-6 shaves. Consequently, I usually wait until the battery needs to be charged before I clean it. However, I remove the foil screen head after each shave and tap-out the razor stubble. This routine has worked just fine, while extending the \\&quot;life\\&quot; of the cleaning fluid. After almost three months, the electronic level indicator still shows the fluid level as \\&quot;high\\&quot;. If you&#x27;re a clean freak, you can clean your shaver more frequently (I&#x27;ve read several reviews from people who do so after every shave), but I believe it&#x27;s overkill. Besides, you&#x27;ll buy considerably more cleaning fluid.    Bottom-line: When it comes to my morning shaving routine, I feel like I have finally arrived! While I am not sure that shaving could ever become pleasurable, this shaver has at least removed the dread from this daily task. Moreover, I can&#x27;t imagine there is another electric shaver on the market that provides a better, quicker and more comfortable shave. I know my wife is probably tired of hearing, \\&quot;Have I told you how much I like this shaver?!\\&quot; This electric shaver is simply the best!</li>

In terms of the quality of the shave, it&#x27;s not as good as a manual razor. It doesn&#x27;t even give me a better shave than my old Norelco, and it takes longer, requires more facial manipulation, and makes a lot more noise than the Norelco. I can&#x27;t see any particular benefit from the touted vibrating head. Perhaps it&#x27;s very slightly more effective at picking up difficult hairs, but I&#x27;m not even sure of that.      Nevertheless, while it is slower and louder than my Norelco, I&#x27;m reasonably satisfied with my purchase, because the cleaning system really does work as advertised. Although the head of my Norelco could be rinsed under running water, to get a really good shave I nevertheless had to disassemble it every couple of weeks and clean the half-dozen fiddly little parts with a brush. The Braun, on the other hand, does indeed seem to give an \\&quot;as new\\&quot; shave consistently if I run the cleaning cycle regularly. That&#x27;s a good thing, because while it still comes with a little brush, there&#x27;s not much you can do with it--the cutters are part of a sealed monolithic head module (which probably means greater expense if it is damaged or worn out, but that hasn&#x27;t happened yet). Moreover, I experience less facial irritation with the Braun, probably because the alcohol-based cleaning solution reduces bacterial contamination. The cleaning cycle is noisy, but actually less so than shaving, because it is muffled a bit by the stand--although it can be disconcerting to hear the thing buzzing away in the bathroom with nobody in there. Disadvantages are that the cleaning solution leaves a residue on the head that smells bad--and tastes even worse if I happen to get it on my lips. And of course you have to periodically replace the cleaning solution (which lasts about a month, as advertised). You can rinse it under running water, which is fine for a short trip. The battery charge is good for over a week--at least now while it&#x27;s still fairly new--and all you need to recharge it is the wire; you can leave the base at home. But I find that running the cleaning cycle regularly gives the best shave.</li>

It is easy to use, easy to clean and just does it&#x27;s thing, flawlessly.  My dad, visiting us this year, agreed, so we purchased another for him this holiday.  Can&#x27;t say much more about our satisfaction except you will NOT be disapointed - well worth the price!</li>
